      <p>
       <b>
        New Orleans
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/nj/: 'n' in 'new'">
            nj
           </span>
           <span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">
            uː
           </span>
          </span>
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">
            ɔːr
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">
            i
           </span>
           <span title="/./: syllable break">
            .
           </span>
           <span title="/ən/: 'on' in 'button'">
            ən
           </span>
           <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
            z
           </span>
          </span>
          , -
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">
            ɔːr
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">
            iː
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
            z
           </span>
          </span>
          , -
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">
            ɔːr
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/ən/: 'on' in 'button'">
            ən
           </span>
           <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
            z
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mw_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mw-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">
            ɔːr
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/ən/: 'on' in 'button'">
            ən
           </span>
           <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
            z
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">
         <b>
          La Nouvelle-Orléans
         </b>
        </span>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">
         [la nuvɛlɔʁleɑ̃]
        </a>
       </span>
       <small class="nowrap">
        (
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:La_Nouvelle-Orleans.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/La_Nouvelle-Orleans.ogg" title="La Nouvelle-Orleans.ogg">
           listen
          </a>
         </span>
        </span>
        )
       </small>
       ) is a
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_ports_in_the_United_States" title="List of ports in the United States">
        major United States
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_New_Orleans" title="Port of New Orleans">
        port
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largest_city" title="Largest city">
        largest city
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Metropolitan_Area" title="New Orleans Metropolitan Area">
        metropolitan area
       </a>
       in the state of
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">
        Louisiana
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The population of the city was 343,829 as of the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">
        2010 U.S. Census
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QF_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-QF-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_metropolitan_area" title="New Orleans metropolitan area">
        New Orleans metropolitan area
       </a>
       (New Orleans–Metairie–Kenner Metropolitan Statistical Area) had a population of 1,167,764 in 2010 and was the 46th largest in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans-Metairie-Bogalusa_combined_statistical_area" title="New Orleans-Metairie-Bogalusa combined statistical area">
        New Orleans–Metairie–Bogalusa Combined Statistical Area
       </a>
       , a larger trading area, had a 2010 population of 1,452,502.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Before
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">
        Hurricane Katrina
       </a>
       , Orleans Parish was the most populous
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_parishes_in_Louisiana" title="List of parishes in Louisiana">
        parish
       </a>
       in Louisiana. As of 2015,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_Department_of_Commerce_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-US_Department_of_Commerce-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       it ranked third, trailing neighboring
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jefferson_Parish" title="Jefferson Parish">
        Jefferson Parish
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/East_Baton_Rouge_Parish,_Louisiana" title="East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana">
        East Baton Rouge Parish
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_Department_of_Commerce_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-US_Department_of_Commerce-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The city is known for its distinct
       <a href="/wiki/French_architecture#America" title="French architecture">
        French and Spanish Creole architecture
       </a>
       , as well as its cross-cultural and multilingual heritage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-multi_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-multi-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       New Orleans is famous for its cuisine, music (particularly as the birthplace of
       <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">
        jazz
       </a>
       )
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pbsjazz_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pbsjazz-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usinfo_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-usinfo-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and its annual celebrations and festivals, most notably
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Mardi_Gras" title="New Orleans Mardi Gras">
         Mardi Gras
        </a>
       </i>
       . The city is often referred to as the "most unique"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mostunique_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mostunique-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gmc_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gmc-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hurrbayou_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hurrbayou-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forusa_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-forusa-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bringback_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bringback-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msn_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-msn-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans is located in southeastern
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">
        Louisiana
       </a>
       , and occupies both sides of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">
        Mississippi River
       </a>
       . The heart of the city and its
       <a href="/wiki/French_Quarter" title="French Quarter">
        French Quarter
       </a>
       is on the river's north side. The city and Orleans Parish (
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">
         paroisse d'Orléans
        </span>
       </i>
       ) are coterminous.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coextensive_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-coextensive-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city and parish are bounded by the parishes of
       <a href="/wiki/St._Tammany_Parish,_Louisiana" title="St. Tammany Parish, Louisiana">
        St. Tammany
       </a>
       to the north,
       <a href="/wiki/St._Bernard_Parish,_Louisiana" title="St. Bernard Parish, Louisiana">
        St. Bernard
       </a>
       to the east,
       <a href="/wiki/Plaquemines_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Plaquemines Parish, Louisiana">
        Plaquemines
       </a>
       to the south, and
       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Jefferson Parish, Louisiana">
        Jefferson
       </a>
       to the south and west.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-coextensive_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-coextensive-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parishmap_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-parishmap-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citycharter_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-citycharter-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pontchartrain" title="Lake Pontchartrain">
        Lake Pontchartrain
       </a>
       , part of lies within the city limits, lies to the north and
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Borgne" title="Lake Borgne">
        Lake Borgne
       </a>
       lies to the east.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citycharter_22-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-citycharter-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Names">
        Names
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:377px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_Skyline.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="1268" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/New_Orleans_Skyline.jpg/375px-New_Orleans_Skyline.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/New_Orleans_Skyline.jpg/563px-New_Orleans_Skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/New_Orleans_Skyline.jpg/750px-New_Orleans_Skyline.jpg 2x" width="375"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_Skyline.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The New Orleans cityscape in early-February 2007
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city is named after
       <a href="/wiki/Philippe_II,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Philippe II, Duke of Orléans">
        the Duke of Orleans
       </a>
       , who reigned as Regent for
       <a href="/wiki/Louis_XV_of_France" title="Louis XV of France">
        Louis XV
       </a>
       from 1715 to 1723. It has many illustrative nicknames:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         Crescent City
        </i>
        alludes to the course of the
        <a href="/wiki/Lower_Mississippi_River" title="Lower Mississippi River">
         Lower Mississippi River
        </a>
        around and through the city.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOCVBnicknames_23-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-NOCVBnicknames-23">
          [23]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         The Big Easy
        </i>
        was possibly
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
           <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2016)">
            clarification needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
        a reference by musicians in the early 20th century to the relative ease of finding work there.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">
           <span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (August 2016)">
            dubious
           </span>
          </a>
          <span class="metadata">
           –
           <a href="/wiki/Talk:New_Orleans#Dubious" title="Talk:New Orleans">
            discuss
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
        It may have originated in the
        <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">
         Prohibition
        </a>
        era, when the city was considered one big
        <a href="/wiki/Speakeasy" title="Speakeasy">
         speakeasy
        </a>
        due to the government's inability to control
        <a href="/wiki/Alcohol" title="Alcohol">
         alcohol
        </a>
        sales in open violation of the
        <a href="/wiki/Eighteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Eighteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">
         18th Amendment
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">
           <span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (August 2016)">
            dubious
           </span>
          </a>
          <span class="metadata">
           –
           <a href="/wiki/Talk:New_Orleans#Dubious" title="Talk:New Orleans">
            discuss
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         The City that Care Forgot
        </i>
        has been used since at least 1938,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
         <a href="#cite_note-24">
          [24]
         </a>
        </sup>
        and refers to the outwardly easy-going, carefree nature of the residents.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_Orleans" title="History of New Orleans">
        History of New Orleans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_New_Orleans" title="Timeline of New Orleans">
        Timeline of New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings">
        Beginnings
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="quotebox pullquote" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:24em; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 90%; background-color: #B0C4DE;">
       <div class="" style="background-color: #B0C4DE; color: black; text-align: center; font-size: larger; font-weight: bold;">
        Historical affiliations
       </div>
       <div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
        <div>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Royal_Standard_of_the_King_of_France.svg/23px-Royal_Standard_of_the_King_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Royal_Standard_of_the_King_of_France.svg/35px-Royal_Standard_of_the_King_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Royal_Standard_of_the_King_of_France.svg/45px-Royal_Standard_of_the_King_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">
          Kingdom of France
         </a>
         1718–1763
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Flag_of_Spain_%281785-1873_and_1875-1931%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain_%281785-1873_and_1875-1931%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Flag_of_Spain_%281785-1873_and_1875-1931%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Spain_%281785-1873_and_1875-1931%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Flag_of_Spain_%281785-1873_and_1875-1931%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Spain_%281785-1873_and_1875-1931%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_in_Spain" title="Enlightenment in Spain">
          Kingdom of Spain
         </a>
         1763–1802
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_France_%281794-1815%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_France_%281794-1815%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_France_%281794-1815%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_France_%281794-1815%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_France_%281794-1815%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_France_%281794-1815%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">
          French First Republic
         </a>
         1802–1803
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </span>
         United States of America 1803–1861
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1382" data-file-width="2161" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Louisiana_%28February_1861%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Louisiana_%28February_1861%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Louisiana_%28February_1861%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Louisiana_%28February_1861%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Louisiana_%28February_1861%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_Louisiana_%28February_1861%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </span>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Louisiana" title="Republic of Louisiana">
          Republic of Louisiana
         </a>
         1861
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Flag_of_the_Confederate_States_of_America_%281865%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Confederate_States_of_America_%281865%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Flag_of_the_Confederate_States_of_America_%281865%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Confederate_States_of_America_%281865%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Flag_of_the_Confederate_States_of_America_%281865%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Confederate_States_of_America_%281865%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">
          Confederate States of America
         </a>
         1861–1862
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
         </span>
         United States of America 1862–present
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       La Nouvelle-Orléans (New Orleans) was founded in Spring of 1718 (7 May has become the traditional date to mark the anniversary, but the actual day is unknown
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) by the
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_Company" title="Mississippi Company">
        French Mississippi Company
       </a>
       , under the direction of
       <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Le_Moyne,_Sieur_de_Bienville" title="Jean-Baptiste Le Moyne, Sieur de Bienville">
        Jean-Baptiste Le Moyne de Bienville
       </a>
       , on land inhabited by the
       <a href="/wiki/Chitimacha" title="Chitimacha">
        Chitimacha
       </a>
       . It was named for
       <a href="/wiki/Philippe_II,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Philippe II, Duke of Orléans">
        Philippe II, Duke of Orléans
       </a>
       , who was
       <a href="/wiki/Regent" title="Regent">
        Regent
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">
        Kingdom of France
       </a>
       at the time. His title came from the French city of
       <a href="/wiki/Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Orléans">
        Orléans
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">
        French colony
       </a>
       was ceded to the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        Spanish Empire
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">
        Treaty of Paris (1763)
       </a>
       . During the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">
        American Revolutionary War
       </a>
       , New Orleans was an important
       <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">
        port
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Smuggling" title="Smuggling">
        smuggling
       </a>
       aid to the
       <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">
        rebels
       </a>
       , transporting military equipment and supplies up the
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">
        Mississippi River
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernardo_de_G%C3%A1lvez_y_Madrid,_Count_of_G%C3%A1lvez" title="Bernardo de Gálvez y Madrid, Count of Gálvez">
        Bernardo de Gálvez y Madrid, Count of Gálvez
       </a>
       successfully launched a southern campaign against the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_army" title="British army">
        British
       </a>
       from the city in 1779.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        Nueva Orleans
       </i>
       (the name of New Orleans in Spanish) remained under Spanish control until 1803, when it reverted briefly to
       <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">
        French
       </a>
       rule. Nearly all of the surviving 18th-century
       <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">
        architecture
       </a>
       of the Vieux Carré (
       <a href="/wiki/French_Quarter" title="French Quarter">
        French Quarter
       </a>
       ) dates from the Spanish period, notably excepting the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Ursuline_Convent" title="Old Ursuline Convent">
        Old Ursuline Convent
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_territory">
        United States territory
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" title="Napoleon I of France">
        Napoleon
       </a>
       sold
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">
        Louisiana (New France)
       </a>
       to the United States in the
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">
        Louisiana Purchase
       </a>
       in 1803. Thereafter, the city grew rapidly with influxes of Americans, French,
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Creole_people" title="Louisiana Creole people">
        Creoles
       </a>
       and Africans. Later immigrants were Irish, Germans and Italians. Major
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commodity_crops" title="Commodity crops">
        commodity crops
       </a>
       of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" title="Sugar cane">
        sugar
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">
        cotton
       </a>
       were cultivated with
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">
        slave
       </a>
       labor on nearby large
       <a href="/wiki/Plantations_in_the_American_South" title="Plantations in the American South">
        plantations
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Thousands of
       <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">
        refugees
       </a>
       from the 1804
       <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">
        Haitian Revolution
       </a>
       , both
       <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">
        whites
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">
        free people of color
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        affranchis
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        gens de couleur libres
       </i>
       ), arrived in New Orleans, often accompanied by
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">
        slaves
       </a>
       of African descent. While Governor
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_C.C._Claiborne" title="William C.C. Claiborne">
        Claiborne
       </a>
       and other officials wanted to keep out additional
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_negro" title="Free negro">
        free black
       </a>
       people, the French Creoles wanted to increase the French-speaking population. As more refugees were allowed into the
       <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Orleans" title="Territory of Orleans">
        Territory of Orleans
       </a>
       , Haitian émigrés who had first gone to
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       also arrived.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AAM_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AAM-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many of the white
       <a href="/wiki/Geographical_distribution_of_French_speakers" title="Geographical distribution of French speakers">
        Francophones
       </a>
       had been deported by officials in Cuba in retaliation for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bonapartist" title="Bonapartist">
        Bonapartist
       </a>
       schemes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGitlin200954_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGitlin200954-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nearly 90 percent of these immigrants settled in New Orleans. The 1809 migration brought 2,731 whites; 3,102 free persons of African descent; and 3,226 slaves of African descent, doubling the city's population. The city became 63 percent black, a greater proportion than
       <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">
        Charleston, South Carolina
       </a>
       's 53 percent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AAM_28-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-AAM-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_New_Orleans">
        Battle of New Orleans
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2579" data-file-width="3488" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg/250px-Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg/375px-Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg/500px-Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_New_Orleans.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_New_Orleans_(1815)" title="Battle of New Orleans (1815)">
          Battle of New Orleans
         </a>
         (1815)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the final campaign of the
       <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">
        War of 1812
       </a>
       , the British sent a force of 11,000 in an attempt to capture New Orleans. Despite great challenges, General
       <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson" title="Andrew Jackson">
        Andrew Jackson
       </a>
       , with support from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy">
        U.S. Navy
       </a>
       , successfully cobbled together a force of:
       <a href="/wiki/Militia" title="Militia">
        militia
       </a>
       from Louisiana and
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_Territory" title="Mississippi Territory">
        Mississippi
       </a>
       , including
       <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">
        free men of color
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Army" title="U.S. Army">
        U.S. Army
       </a>
       regulars, a large contingent of
       <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">
        Tennessee
       </a>
       state
       <a href="/wiki/Militia" title="Militia">
        militia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">
        Kentucky
       </a>
       riflemen,
       <a href="/wiki/Choctaw" title="Choctaw">
        Choctaw
       </a>
       fighters and local
       <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">
        privateers
       </a>
       (the latter led by the pirate
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lafitte" title="Jean Lafitte">
        Jean Lafitte
       </a>
       ), to decisively defeat the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_army" title="British army">
        British troops
       </a>
       , led by
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Pakenham" title="Edward Pakenham">
        Sir Edward Pakenham
       </a>
       , in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_New_Orleans" title="Battle of New Orleans">
        Battle of New Orleans
       </a>
       on January 8, 1815.
      </p>
      <p>
       The armies had not learned of the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Ghent" title="Treaty of Ghent">
        Treaty of Ghent
       </a>
       that had been signed on December 24, 1814 (however, the treaty did not call for cessation of hostilities until after both governments had ratified it. The U.S. government ratified it on February 16, 1815).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Groom2007_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Groom2007-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The fighting in Louisiana had begun in December 1814 and did not end until late January, after the Americans held off the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Navy" title="British Navy">
        British Navy
       </a>
       during a ten-day
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Fort_St._Philip_(1815)" title="Siege of Fort St. Philip (1815)">
        siege of Fort St. Philip
       </a>
       (the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        Royal
       </a>
       Navy went on to capture
       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Bowyer" title="Fort Bowyer">
        Fort Bowyer
       </a>
       near
       <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">
        Mobile
       </a>
       , before the commanders received news of the peace treaty).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Port">
        Port
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hippolyte_Sebron_-_Bateaux_A_Vapeur_G%C3%A9ants_1853.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="555" data-file-width="910" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Hippolyte_Sebron_-_Bateaux_A_Vapeur_G%C3%A9ants_1853.jpg/250px-Hippolyte_Sebron_-_Bateaux_A_Vapeur_G%C3%A9ants_1853.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Hippolyte_Sebron_-_Bateaux_A_Vapeur_G%C3%A9ants_1853.jpg/375px-Hippolyte_Sebron_-_Bateaux_A_Vapeur_G%C3%A9ants_1853.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Hippolyte_Sebron_-_Bateaux_A_Vapeur_G%C3%A9ants_1853.jpg/500px-Hippolyte_Sebron_-_Bateaux_A_Vapeur_G%C3%A9ants_1853.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hippolyte_Sebron_-_Bateaux_A_Vapeur_G%C3%A9ants_1853.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Mississippi River
         <a href="/wiki/Steamboats_of_the_Mississippi" title="Steamboats of the Mississippi">
          steamboats
         </a>
         at New Orleans, 1853
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       As a
       <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">
        port
       </a>
       New Orleans played a major role during the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Southern_United_States" title="History of the Southern United States">
        antebellum
       </a>
       era in the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">
        Atlantic slave trade
       </a>
       . The port handled commodities for export from the interior and imported goods from other countries, which were warehoused and transferred in New Orleans to smaller vessels and distributed along the
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">
        Mississippi River
       </a>
       watershed. The river was filled with steamboats, flatboats and sailing ships. Despite its role in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">
        slave trade
       </a>
       , New Orleans at the time had the largest and most prosperous community of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_persons_of_color" title="Free persons of color">
        free persons of color
       </a>
       in the nation, who were often educated, middle-class property owners.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pbsjazz_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-pbsjazz-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Slavery_and_immigration">
        Slavery and immigration
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Dwarfing the other cities in the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Southern_United_States" title="History of the Southern United States">
        antebellum South
       </a>
       , New Orleans had the nation's largest slave market. The market expanded after the U.S. ended the international
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">
        trade
       </a>
       in 1808. Two-thirds of the more than one million slaves brought to the
       <a href="/wiki/Deep_South" title="Deep South">
        Deep South
       </a>
       arrived via
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forced_migration" title="Forced migration">
        forced migration
       </a>
       in the domestic
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">
        slave trade
       </a>
       . The money generated by the sale of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slaves" title="Slaves">
        slaves
       </a>
       in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_South" title="Upper South">
        Upper South
       </a>
       has been estimated at 15 percent of the value of the staple crop economy. The
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">
        slaves
       </a>
       were collectively valued at half a billion dollars. An ancillary economy grew up around the trade—for transportation, housing and clothing, fees, etc., estimated at 13.5% of the price per person, amounting to tens of billions of dollars (2005 dollars, adjusted for inflation) during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plantation_era" title="Plantation era">
        antebellum period
       </a>
       , with New Orleans as a prime beneficiary.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to historian Paul Lachance,
      </p>
      <table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
       <tr>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">
         “
        </td>
        <td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">
         the addition of white immigrants [from Saint-Domingue] to the white creole population enabled French-speakers to remain a majority of the white population until almost 1830. If a substantial proportion of free persons of color and slaves had not also spoken French, however, the
         <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">
          Gallic
         </a>
         community would have become a minority of the total population as early as 1820.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGitlin2009159_33-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGitlin2009159-33">
           [33]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">
         ”
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       After the Louisiana Purchase, numerous
       <a href="/wiki/English_Americans" title="English Americans">
        Anglo-Americans
       </a>
       migrated to the city. The population doubled in the 1830s and by 1840, New Orleans had become the nation's wealthiest and the third-most populous city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       German and Irish immigrants began arriving in the 1840s, working as port laborers. In this period, the state legislature passed more restrictions on
       <a href="/wiki/Manumission" title="Manumission">
        manumissions
       </a>
       of slaves and virtually ended it in 1852.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manumission_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-manumission-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 1850s, white Francophones remained an intact and vibrant community. They maintained instruction in French in two of the city's four school districts (all were white).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGitlin2009166_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGitlin2009166-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1860, the city had 13,000
       <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">
        free people of color
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        gens de couleur libres
       </i>
       ), the class of free, mostly
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed-race" title="Mixed-race">
        mixed-race
       </a>
       people that expanded during French and Spanish rule. The census recorded 81 percent as mulatto, a term used to cover all degrees of mixed race.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manumission_35-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-manumission-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Mostly part of the Francophone group, they constituted the artisan, educated and professional class of African Americans. Most blacks were still enslaved, working at the port, in domestic service, in crafts, and mostly on the many large, surrounding
       <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">
        sugarcane
       </a>
       plantations.
      </p>
      <p>
       After growing by 45 percent in the 1850s, by 1860, the city had nearly 170,000 people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nystrom_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nystrom-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It had grown in wealth, with a "per capita income [that] was second in the nation and the highest in the South."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nystrom_37-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-nystrom-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city had a role as the "primary commercial gateway for the nation's booming mid-section."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nystrom_37-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-nystrom-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The port was the nation's third largest in terms of tonnage of imported goods, after Boston and New York, handling 659,000 tons in 1859.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nystrom_37-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-nystrom-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War">
        Civil War
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="New Orleans in the American Civil War">
        New Orleans in the American Civil War
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:StarvingNewOrleans.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2419" data-file-width="3515" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/StarvingNewOrleans.jpg/250px-StarvingNewOrleans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/StarvingNewOrleans.jpg/375px-StarvingNewOrleans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/StarvingNewOrleans.jpg/500px-StarvingNewOrleans.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:StarvingNewOrleans.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The starving people of New Orleans under Union occupation during the Civil War, 1862
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       As the Creole elite feared, the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">
        Civil War
       </a>
       changed their world. In 1862, following the occupation by the Navy after the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Forts_Jackson_and_St._Philip" title="Battle of Forts Jackson and St. Philip">
        Battle of Forts Jackson and St. Philip
       </a>
       , led by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benjamin_Butler_(politician)" title="Benjamin Butler (politician)">
        Gen. Benjamin F. Butler
       </a>
       , a respected state lawyer of the Massachusetts militia, Northern forces occupied the city. Later New Orleans residents nicknamed him "Beast" Butler, because of a military order he issued. After his troops had been assaulted and harassed in the streets by Southern women, his order warned that future such occurrences would result in his men treating such "ladies" as those "plying their avocation in the streets", implying that they would treat the women like prostitutes. Accounts of this spread widely. He also came to be called "Spoons" Butler because of the alleged looting that his troops did while occupying the city.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Butler abolished French language instruction in city schools. Statewide measures in 1864 and, after the war, 1868 further strengthened the English-only policy imposed by federal representatives. With the predominance of English speakers, that language had already become dominant in business and government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGitlin2009166_36-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGitlin2009166-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the end of the 19th century, French usage had faded. It was also under pressure from Irish, Italian and German immigrants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGitlin2009180_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGitlin2009180-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, as late as 1902 "one-fourth of the population of the city spoke French in ordinary daily intercourse, while another two-fourths was able to understand the language perfectly,"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and as late as 1945, many elderly Creole women spoke no English.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The last major French language newspaper,
       <i>
        L'Abeille de la Nouvelle-Orléans
       </i>
       (New Orleans Bee), ceased publication on December 27, 1923, after ninety-six years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brasseaux2005_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brasseaux2005-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (According to some sources,
       <i>
        Le Courrier de la Nouvelle Orleans
       </i>
       continued until 1955.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       )
      </p>
      <p>
       As the city was captured and occupied early in the war, it was spared the destruction through warfare suffered by many other cities of the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">
        American South
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">
        Union Army
       </a>
       eventually extended its control north along the
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">
        Mississippi River
       </a>
       and along the coastal areas. As a result, most of the southern portion of Louisiana was originally exempted from the liberating provisions of the 1863 "
       <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_Proclamation" title="Emancipation Proclamation">
        Emancipation Proclamation
       </a>
       " issued by President
       <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">
        Abraham Lincoln
       </a>
       . Large numbers of rural ex-slaves and some free people of color from the city volunteered for the first regiments of Black troops in the War. Led by Brigadier General
       <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Ullman" title="Daniel Ullman">
        Daniel Ullman
       </a>
       (1810–1892), of the 78th Regiment of New York State Volunteers Militia, they were known as the "
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Colored_Troops" title="United States Colored Troops">
        Corps d'Afrique
       </a>
       ." While that name had been used by a militia before the war, that group was composed of
       <a href="/wiki/Free_people_of_color" title="Free people of color">
        free people of color
       </a>
       . The new group was made up mostly of former slaves. They were supplemented in the last two years of the War by newly organized
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Colored_Troops" title="United States Colored Troops">
        United States Colored Troops
       </a>
       , who played an increasingly important part in the war.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reconstruction">
        Reconstruction
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Violence throughout the South, especially the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memphis_Riots_of_1866" title="Memphis Riots of 1866">
        Memphis Riots of 1866
       </a>
       followed by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Riot" title="New Orleans Riot">
        New Orleans Riot
       </a>
       in the same year, led Congress to passi the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Act" title="Reconstruction Act">
        Reconstruction Act
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Fourteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">
        Fourteenth Amendment
       </a>
       , exten
       <a href="/wiki/Fourteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">
        ing
       </a>
       d the protections of full citizenship to freedmen and free people of color. Louisiana and Texas were put under the authority of the"
       <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Military_District" title="Fifth Military District">
        Fifth Military District
       </a>
       " of the United States during Reconstruction. Louisiana was readmitted to the Union in 1868. Its Constitution of 1868 granted
       <a href="/wiki/Universal_manhood_suffrage" title="Universal manhood suffrage">
        universal male suffrage
       </a>
       and established universal
       <a href="/wiki/State_school" title="State school">
        public education
       </a>
       . Both blacks and whites were elected to local and state offices. In 1872, lieutenant governor
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P.B.S._Pinchback" title="P.B.S. Pinchback">
        P.B.S. Pinchback
       </a>
       , who was of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed_race" title="Mixed race">
        mixed race
       </a>
       , succeeded
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_C._Warmouth" title="Henry C. Warmouth">
        Henry Clay Warmouth
       </a>
       for a brief period as Republican governor of
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">
        Louisiana
       </a>
       , becoming the first governor of African descent of an
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">
        American state
       </a>
       (the next African American to serve as governor of an American state was
       <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Wilder" title="Douglas Wilder">
        Douglas Wilder
       </a>
       , elected in Virginia in 1989). New Orleans operated a racially-integrated
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Public_Schools" title="New Orleans Public Schools">
        public school system
       </a>
       during this period.
      </p>
      <p>
       Wartime damage to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Levees" title="Levees">
        levees
       </a>
       and cities along the Mississippi River adversely affected southern crops and trade. The federal government contributed to restoring infrastructure. The nationwide financial recession and
       <a href="/wiki/Panic_of_1873" title="Panic of 1873">
        Panic of 1873
       </a>
       adversely affected businesses and slowed economic recovery.
      </p>
      <p>
       From 1868, elections in Louisiana were marked by violence, as white insurgents tried to suppress black voting and disrupt
       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
        Republican Party
       </a>
       gatherings. Violence continued around elections. The disputed 1872 gubernatorial election resulted in conflicts that ran for years. The "
       <a href="/wiki/White_League" title="White League">
        White League
       </a>
       ", an insurgent paramilitary group that supported the
       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">
        Democratic Party
       </a>
       , was organized in 1874 and operated in the open, violently suppressing the black vote and running off Republican officeholders. In 1874, in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Liberty_Place" title="Battle of Liberty Place">
        Battle of Liberty Place
       </a>
       , 5,000 members of the White League fought with city police to take over the state offices for the Democrati candidate for governor, holding them for three days. By 1876, such tactics resulted in the white
       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">
        Democrats
       </a>
       , the so-called
       <a href="/wiki/Redeemers" title="Redeemers">
        Redeemers
       </a>
       , regaining political control of the state legislature. The federal government gave up and withdrew its troops in 1877, ending
       <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Era" title="Reconstruction Era">
        Reconstruction
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Jim_Crow_era">
        Jim Crow era
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       White Democrats passed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jim_Crow" title="Jim Crow">
        Jim Crow
       </a>
       laws, establishing
       <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">
        racial segregation
       </a>
       in public facilities. In 1889, the legislature passed a
       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_amendment" title="Constitutional amendment">
        constitutional amendment
       </a>
       incorporating a "
       <a href="/wiki/Grandfather_clause" title="Grandfather clause">
        grandfather clause
       </a>
       " that effectively
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disfranchisement_after_Reconstruction_era" title="Disfranchisement after Reconstruction era">
        disfranchised
       </a>
       freedmen as well as the propertied people of color manumitted before the war. Unable to vote, African Americans could not serve on juries or in local office, and were closed out of formal politics for generations. The South was ruled by a white Democratic Party. Public schools were
       <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">
        racially segregated
       </a>
       and remained so until 1960.
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans' large community of well-educated, often French-speaking
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_persons_of_color" title="Free persons of color">
        free persons of color
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        gens de couleur libres
       </i>
       ), who had been free prior to the Civil War, fought against Jim Crow. They organized the
       <i>
        Comité des Citoyens
       </i>
       (Citizens Committee) to work for civil rights. As part of their legal campaign, they recruited one of their own,
       <a href="/wiki/Homer_Plessy" title="Homer Plessy">
        Homer Plessy
       </a>
       , to test whether Louisiana's newly enacted Separate Car Act was constitutional. Plessy boarded a commuter train departing New Orleans for
       <a href="/wiki/Covington,_Louisiana" title="Covington, Louisiana">
        Covington, Louisiana
       </a>
       , sat in the car reserved for whites only, and was arrested. The case resulting from this incident,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Plessy_v._Ferguson" title="Plessy v. Ferguson">
         Plessy v. Ferguson
        </a>
       </i>
       , was heard by the
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">
        U.S. Supreme Court
       </a>
       in 1896. The court ruled that "
       <a href="/wiki/Separate_but_equal" title="Separate but equal">
        separate but equal
       </a>
       " accommodations were constitutional, effectively upholding Jim Crow measures. In practice, African-American public schools and facilities were underfunded across the South. The Supreme Court ruling contributed to this period as the
       <a href="/wiki/Nadir_of_American_race_relations" title="Nadir of American race relations">
        nadir of race relations
       </a>
       in the United States. The rate of
       <a href="/wiki/Lynching_in_the_United_States" title="Lynching in the United States">
        lynchings
       </a>
       of black men was high across the South, as other states also disfranchised blacks and sought to impose Jim Crow.
       <a href="/wiki/Anti-Italianism#Anti-Italianism_in_the_United_States" title="Anti-Italianism">
        Anti-Italian
       </a>
       sentiment in 1891 contributed to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/March_14,_1891_lynchings" title="March 14, 1891 lynchings">
        lynchings of 11 Italians
       </a>
       , some of whom had been acquitted of the murder of the police chief. Some were shot and killed in the jail where they were detained. It was the largest mass lynching in U.S. history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gambino2000_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gambino2000-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In July 1900 the city was swept by white mobs rioting after Robert Charles, a young African American, killed a policeman and temporarily escaped. They killed him and an estimated 20 other blacks; seven whites died in the days-long conflict, until a
       <a href="/wiki/Militia_(United_States)" title="Militia (United States)">
        state militia
       </a>
       suppressed it.
      </p>
      <p>
       Throughout New Orleans' history, until the early 20th century when medical and scientific advances ameliorated the situation, the city suffered repeated
       <a href="/wiki/Epidemic" title="Epidemic">
        epidemics
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">
        yellow fever
       </a>
       and other tropical and
       <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">
        infectious diseases
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">
        20th century
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EsplanadeBurgundy1900.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7622" data-file-width="9648" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/EsplanadeBurgundy1900.jpg/220px-EsplanadeBurgundy1900.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/EsplanadeBurgundy1900.jpg/330px-EsplanadeBurgundy1900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/EsplanadeBurgundy1900.jpg/440px-EsplanadeBurgundy1900.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EsplanadeBurgundy1900.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Esplanade_Avenue,_New_Orleans" title="Esplanade Avenue, New Orleans">
          Esplanade Avenue
         </a>
         at Burgundy Street, looking lakewards north towards
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Ponchartrain" title="Lake Ponchartrain">
          Lake Ponchartrain
         </a>
         (1900)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RationingBoardNOLAVachonC.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4108" data-file-width="4145" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/RationingBoardNOLAVachonC.jpg/220px-RationingBoardNOLAVachonC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/RationingBoardNOLAVachonC.jpg/330px-RationingBoardNOLAVachonC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/RationingBoardNOLAVachonC.jpg/440px-RationingBoardNOLAVachonC.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RationingBoardNOLAVachonC.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         1943 waiting line at wartime Rationing Board office in New Orleans
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans' zenith versus other American cities occurred in the ante-bellum period. It was the nation's fifth-largest city and was significantly larger than all other southern cities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis-2003–175_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lewis-2003–175-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From the mid-19th century onward rapid economic growth shifted to other areas, while New Orleans' relative importance steadily declined. The growth of railways and highways decreased river traffic, diverting goods to other transportation corridors and markets.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis-2003–175_46-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lewis-2003–175-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Thousands of the most ambitious
       <a href="/wiki/Person_of_color" title="Person of color">
        people of color
       </a>
       left the state in the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">
        Great Migration
       </a>
       around
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       and after, many for
       <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">
        West Coast
       </a>
       destinations. From the late 1800s, most censuses recorded New Orleans' decline versus other American cities.
      </p>
      <p>
       By the mid-20th century, New Orleanians recognized that their city was no longer the leading urban area in the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">
        South
       </a>
       . By 1950,
       <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">
        Houston
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">
        Dallas
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">
        Atlanta
       </a>
       exceeded New Orleans in size, and in 1960
       <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">
        Miami
       </a>
       eclipsed New Orleans, even as the latter's population reached its historic peak.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lewis-2003–175_46-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lewis-2003–175-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As with other older American cities, highway construction and suburban development drew residents from the center city to newer housing outside. The 1970 census recorded the first absolute decline in population since it joined the United States. The
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_metropolitan_area" title="New Orleans metropolitan area">
        New Orleans metropolitan area
       </a>
       continued expanding in population, albeit more slowly than other major Sun Belt cities. While the
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_New_Orleans" title="Port of New Orleans">
        port
       </a>
       remained one of the nation's largest, automation and
       <a href="/wiki/Containerization" title="Containerization">
        containerization
       </a>
       cost many jobs. The city's former role as banker to the South was supplanted by larger peer cities. New Orleans' economy had always been based more on trade and financial services than on manufacturing, but the city's relatively small manufacturing sector also shrank after World War II. Despite some economic development successes under the administrations of
       <a href="/wiki/DeLesseps_Story_Morrison" title="DeLesseps Story Morrison">
        DeLesseps "Chep" Morrison
       </a>
       (1946–1961) and
       <a href="/wiki/Victor_H._Schiro" title="Victor H. Schiro">
        Victor "Vic" Schiro
       </a>
       (1961–1970), metropolitan New Orleans' growth rate consistently lagged behind more vigorous cities.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_Rights_Movement">
        Civil Rights Movement
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       During the later years of Morrison's administration, and for the entirety of Schiro's, the city was a center of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Movement" title="Civil Rights Movement">
        Civil Rights Movement
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Christian_Leadership_Conference" title="Southern Christian Leadership Conference">
        Southern Christian Leadership Conference
       </a>
       was founded there, and lunch counter sit-ins were held in
       <a href="/wiki/Canal_Street,_New_Orleans" title="Canal Street, New Orleans">
        Canal Street
       </a>
       department stores. A prominent and violent series of confrontations occurred in 1960 when the city attempted school desegregation, following the Supreme Court ruling in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Brown_v._Board_of_Education" title="Brown v. Board of Education">
         Brown v. Board of Education
        </a>
       </i>
       (1954). When six-year-old
       <a href="/wiki/Ruby_Bridges" title="Ruby Bridges">
        Ruby Bridges
       </a>
       integrated William Frantz Elementary School in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ninth_Ward_of_New_Orleans" title="Ninth Ward of New Orleans">
        Ninth Ward
       </a>
       , she was the first child of color to attend a previously all-white school in the South.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Civil Rights Movement's success in gaining federal passage of the
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">
        Civil Rights Act of 1964
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Voting_Rights_Act_of_1965" title="Voting Rights Act of 1965">
        Voting Rights Act of 1965
       </a>
       renewed constitutional rights, including voting for blacks. Together, these resulted in the most far-reaching changes in New Orleans' 20th century history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Though legal and civil equality were re-established by the end of the 1960s, a large gap in income levels and educational attainment persisted between the city's White and African-American communities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As the middle class and wealthier members of both races left the center city, its population's income level dropped, and it became proportionately more African American. From 1980, the African-American majority elected primarily officials from its own community. They struggled to narrow the gap by creating conditions conducive to the economic uplift of the African-American community.
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans became increasingly dependent on tourism as an economic mainstay during the administrations of
       <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Barthelemy" title="Sidney Barthelemy">
        Sidney Barthelemy
       </a>
       (1986–1994) and
       <a href="/wiki/Marc_Morial" title="Marc Morial">
        Marc Morial
       </a>
       (1994–2002). Relatively low levels of educational attainment, high rates of household poverty, and rising crime threatened the prosperity in the later decades of the century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_48-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The negative effects of these socioeconomic conditions contrasted with the changes to the economy of the United States, which reflected a post-industrial, knowledge-based paradigm in which mental skills and education were more important to advancement than manual skills.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Drainage_and_flood_control">
        Drainage and flood control
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Drainage_in_New_Orleans" title="Drainage in New Orleans">
        Drainage in New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LPD18USSNewOrleansPassingNewOrleans.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="526" data-file-width="799" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/LPD18USSNewOrleansPassingNewOrleans.jpg/250px-LPD18USSNewOrleansPassingNewOrleans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/LPD18USSNewOrleansPassingNewOrleans.jpg/375px-LPD18USSNewOrleansPassingNewOrleans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/LPD18USSNewOrleansPassingNewOrleans.jpg/500px-LPD18USSNewOrleansPassingNewOrleans.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LPD18USSNewOrleansPassingNewOrleans.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A view of the
         <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Central_Business_District" title="New Orleans Central Business District">
          New Orleans Central Business District
         </a>
         as seen from the
         <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">
          Mississippi River
         </a>
         .
         <a href="/wiki/USS_New_Orleans_(LPD-18)" title="USS New Orleans (LPD-18)">
          USS
          <i>
           New Orleans
          </i>
          (LPD-18)
         </a>
         in foreground (2007)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the 20th century, New Orleans' government and business leaders believed they needed to drain and develop outlying areas to provide for the city's expansion. The most ambitious development during this period was a drainage plan devised by engineer and inventor
       <a href="/wiki/A._Baldwin_Wood" title="A. Baldwin Wood">
        A. Baldwin Wood
       </a>
       , designed to break the surrounding swamp's stranglehold on the city's geographic expansion. Until then, urban development in New Orleans was largely limited to higher ground along the natural river levees and
       <a href="/wiki/Bayou" title="Bayou">
        bayous
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Wood's pump system allowed the city to drain huge tracts of swamp and marshland and expand into low-lying areas. Over the 20th century, rapid
       <a href="/wiki/Subsidence" title="Subsidence">
        subsidence
       </a>
       , both natural and human-induced, resulted in these newly populated areas declining to several feet below sea level.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans was vulnerable to flooding even before the city's footprint departed from the natural high ground near the Mississippi River. In the late 20th century, however, scientists and New Orleans residents gradually became aware of the city's increased vulnerability. In 1965, flooding from
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Betsy" title="Hurricane Betsy">
        Hurricane Betsy
       </a>
       killed dozens of residents, although the majority of the city remained dry. The rain-induced
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/May_8th_1995_Louisiana_Flood" title="May 8th 1995 Louisiana Flood">
        flood of May 8, 1995
       </a>
       , demonstrated the weakness of the pumping system. After that event, measures were undertaken to dramatically upgrade pumping capacity. By the 1980s and 1990s, scientists observed that extensive, rapid, and ongoing
       <a href="/wiki/Coastal_erosion" title="Coastal erosion">
        erosion of the marshlands and swamp surrounding New Orleans
       </a>
       , especially that related to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mississippi_River_%E2%80%93_Gulf_Outlet_Canal" title="Mississippi River – Gulf Outlet Canal">
        Mississippi River – Gulf Outlet Canal
       </a>
       , had the unintended result of leaving the city more vulnerable to hurricane-induced catastrophic
       <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">
        storm surges
       </a>
       than before.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">
        21st century
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Katrina">
        Hurricane Katrina
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2086" data-file-width="2062" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg/220px-Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg/330px-Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg/440px-Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">
          Hurricane Katrina
         </a>
         at its New Orleans landfall.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Katrina_in_New_Orleans" title="Effects of Hurricane Katrina in New Orleans">
        Effects of Hurricane Katrina in New Orleans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Drainage_in_New_Orleans" title="Drainage in New Orleans">
        Drainage in New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans was catastrophically affected by what Raymond B. Seed called "the worst engineering disaster in the world since
       <a href="/wiki/Chernobyl_disaster" title="Chernobyl disaster">
        Chernobyl
       </a>
       ", when
       <a href="/wiki/2005_levee_failures_in_Greater_New_Orleans" title="2005 levee failures in Greater New Orleans">
        the Federal levee system failed
       </a>
