       during
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">
        Hurricane Katrina
       </a>
       in 2005.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baker_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Baker-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the time the hurricane approached the city at the end of August 2005, most residents had evacuated. As the hurricane passed through the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="Gulf Coast of the United States">
        Gulf Coast region
       </a>
       , the city's
       <a href="/wiki/Flood_Control_Act_of_1965" title="Flood Control Act of 1965">
        federal flood protection
       </a>
       system failed, resulting in the worst
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">
        civil engineering
       </a>
       disaster in American history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Floodwalls and
       <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">
        levees
       </a>
       constructed by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">
        United States Army Corps of Engineers
       </a>
       failed below design specifications and 80% of the city flooded. Tens of thousands of residents who had remained were rescued or otherwise made their way to shelters of last resort at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louisiana_Superdome" title="Louisiana Superdome">
        Louisiana Superdome
       </a>
       or the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Morial_Convention_Center" title="New Orleans Morial Convention Center">
        New Orleans Morial Convention Center
       </a>
       . More than 1,500 people were recorded as having died in Louisiana, most in New Orleans, while others remain unaccounted for.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184_Katrina1_54-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-184_Katrina1-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Before Hurricane Katrina, the city called for the first mandatory evacuation in its history, to be followed by another mandatory evacuation three years later with
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gustav" title="Hurricane Gustav">
        Hurricane Gustav
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Rita">
        Hurricane Rita
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Rita" title="Hurricane Rita">
        Hurricane Rita
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city was declared off-limits to residents while efforts to clean up after
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">
        Hurricane Katrina
       </a>
       began. The approach of
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Rita" title="Hurricane Rita">
        Hurricane Rita
       </a>
       in September 2005 caused repopulation efforts to be postponed,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Ninth_Ward" title="Lower Ninth Ward">
        Lower Ninth Ward
       </a>
       was reflooded by Rita's storm surge.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184_Katrina1_54-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-184_Katrina1-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-disaster_recovery">
        Post-disaster recovery
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_of_New_Orleans" title="Reconstruction of New Orleans">
        Reconstruction of New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Navy-FloodedNewOrleans.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1850" data-file-width="2878" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Navy-FloodedNewOrleans.jpg/220px-Navy-FloodedNewOrleans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Navy-FloodedNewOrleans.jpg/330px-Navy-FloodedNewOrleans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Navy-FloodedNewOrleans.jpg/440px-Navy-FloodedNewOrleans.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Navy-FloodedNewOrleans.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An aerial view from a United States Navy helicopter showing floodwaters around the Louisiana Superdome (stadium) and surrounding area (2005).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Because of the scale of damage, many people resettled permanently outside the area. Federal, state, and local efforts supported recovery and rebuilding in severely damaged neighborhoods. The Census Bureau in July 2006 estimated the population to be 223,000; a subsequent study estimated that 32,000 additional residents had moved to the city as of March 2007, bringing the estimated population to 255,000, approximately 56% of the pre-Katrina population level. Another estimate, based on utility usage from July 2007, estimated the population to be approximately 274,000 or 60% of the pre-Katrina population. These estimates are somewhat smaller to a third estimate, based on mail delivery records, from the Greater New Orleans Community Data Center in June 2007, which indicated that the city had regained approximately two-thirds of its pre-Katrina population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2008, the Census Bureau revised its population estimate for the city upward, to 336,644.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Orleans_2010_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-New_Orleans_2010-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most recently, 2010 estimates show that neighborhoods that did not flood are near or greater than 100% of their pre-Katrina populations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_58-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Several major tourist events and other forms of revenue for the city have returned. Large conventions returned.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       College bowl games returned for the 2006–2007 season. The
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Saints" title="New Orleans Saints">
        New Orleans Saints
       </a>
       returned that season. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Hornets" title="New Orleans Hornets">
        New Orleans Hornets
       </a>
       (now named the Pelicans) returned to the city for the 2007–2008 season. New Orleans hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/2008_NBA_All-Star_Game" title="2008 NBA All-Star Game">
        2008 NBA All-Star Game
       </a>
       . Additionally, the city hosted
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVII" title="Super Bowl XLVII">
        Super Bowl XLVII
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Major annual events such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Mardi_Gras" title="New Orleans Mardi Gras">
        Mardi Gras
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Jazz_%26_Heritage_Festival" title="New Orleans Jazz &amp; Heritage Festival">
        Jazz &amp; Heritage Festival
       </a>
       were never displaced or canceled. A new annual festival, "The Running of the Bulls New Orleans", was created in 2007.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On February 7, 2017,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/February_2017_New_Orleans_tornado" title="February 2017 New Orleans tornado">
        a large EF3 wedge tornado
       </a>
       hit parts of the eastern side of the city, damaging homes and other buildings, as well as destroying a mobile home park. At least 25 people were left injured by the event.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Landsat_new_orleans_nfl.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="405" data-file-width="540" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Landsat_new_orleans_nfl.jpg/250px-Landsat_new_orleans_nfl.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Landsat_new_orleans_nfl.jpg/375px-Landsat_new_orleans_nfl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Landsat_new_orleans_nfl.jpg/500px-Landsat_new_orleans_nfl.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Landsat_new_orleans_nfl.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A true-color satellite image taken on
         <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
          NASA
         </a>
         's
         <a href="/wiki/Landsat_7" title="Landsat 7">
          Landsat 7
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans is located in the
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River_Delta" title="Mississippi River Delta">
        Mississippi River Delta
       </a>
       , south of
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pontchartrain" title="Lake Pontchartrain">
        Lake Pontchartrain
       </a>
       , on the banks of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">
        Mississippi River
       </a>
       , approximately 105 miles (169 km) upriver from the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">
        Gulf of Mexico
       </a>
       . According to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">
        U.S. Census Bureau
       </a>
       , the city's area is 350 square miles (910 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ), of which 169 square miles (440 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) is land and 181 square miles (470 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) (52%) is water.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Orleans Parish is the smallest parish by land area in Louisiana. The area along the river is characterized by ridges and hollows.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Elevation">
        Elevation
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Drainage_in_New_Orleans" title="Drainage in New Orleans">
        Drainage in New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_Levee_System.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="538" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/New_Orleans_Levee_System.svg/250px-New_Orleans_Levee_System.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/New_Orleans_Levee_System.svg/375px-New_Orleans_Levee_System.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/New_Orleans_Levee_System.svg/500px-New_Orleans_Levee_System.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_Levee_System.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Vertical cross-section, showing maximum levee height of 23 feet (7.0 m)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans was originally settled on the river's natural
       <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">
        levees
       </a>
       or high ground. After the
       <a href="/wiki/Flood_Control_Act_of_1965" title="Flood Control Act of 1965">
        Flood Control Act of 1965
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">
        US Army Corps of Engineers
       </a>
       built floodwalls and man-made
       <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">
        levees
       </a>
       around a much larger geographic footprint that included previous marshland and swamp. Over time, pumping of water from marshland allowed for development into lower elevation areas. Today, a large portion of the city is at or below local mean sea level. Evidence suggests that portions of the city may be dropping in elevation due to
       <a href="/wiki/Subsidence" title="Subsidence">
        subsidence
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Being that the motion of the earth’s surface is shifting downwards relative to sea level.
      </p>
      <p>
       A 2007 study by
       <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">
        Tulane
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Xavier_University_of_Louisiana" title="Xavier University of Louisiana">
        Xavier University
       </a>
       suggested that "51%... of the contiguous urbanized portions of Orleans, Jefferson, and St. Bernard parishes lie at or above sea level," with the more densely populated areas generally on higher ground. The average elevation of the city is currently between 1 foot (0.30 m) and 2 feet (0.61 m) below sea level, with some portions of the city as high as 20 feet (6 m) at the base of the river levee in
       <a href="/wiki/Uptown,_New_Orleans" title="Uptown, New Orleans">
        Uptown
       </a>
       and others as low as 7 feet (2 m) below sea level in the farthest reaches of
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_New_Orleans" title="Eastern New Orleans">
        Eastern New Orleans
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A study published by the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Civil_Engineers" title="American Society of Civil Engineers">
        ASCE
       </a>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Hydrologic_Engineering" title="Journal of Hydrologic Engineering">
         Journal of Hydrologic Engineering
        </a>
       </i>
       in 2016, however, stated:
      </p>
      <table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
       <tr>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">
         “
        </td>
        <td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">
         ...most of New Orleans proper – about 65% – is at or below mean sea level, as defined by the average elevation of Lake Pontchartrain
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
          <a href="#cite_note-67">
           [67]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">
         ”
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The magnitude of
       <a href="/wiki/Subsidence" title="Subsidence">
        subsidence
       </a>
       potentially caused by the draining of natural marsh in the New Orleans area and southeast Louisiana is a topic of debate. A study published in
       <a href="/wiki/Geology_(journal)" title="Geology (journal)">
        <i>
         Geology
        </i>
       </a>
       in 2006 by an associate professor at
       <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">
        Tulane University
       </a>
       claims:
      </p>
      <table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
       <tr>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">
         “
        </td>
        <td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">
         While erosion and wetland loss are huge problems along Louisiana's coast, the basement 30 feet (9.1 m) to 50 feet (15 m) beneath much of the Mississippi Delta has been highly stable for the past 8,000 years with negligible subsidence rates.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
          <a href="#cite_note-68">
           [68]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">
         ”
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The study noted, however, that the results did not necessarily apply to the Mississippi River Delta, nor the New Orleans Metropolitan area proper. On the other hand, a report by the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Civil_Engineers" title="American Society of Civil Engineers">
        American Society of Civil Engineers
       </a>
       claims that "New Orleans is subsiding (sinking)":
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ASCE_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ASCE-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
       <tr>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">
         “
        </td>
        <td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">
         Large portions of Orleans,
         <a href="/wiki/St._Bernard_Parish,_Louisiana" title="St. Bernard Parish, Louisiana">
          St. Bernard
         </a>
         , and
         <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Jefferson Parish, Louisiana">
          Jefferson
         </a>
         parishes are currently below sea level—and continue to sink. New Orleans is built on thousands of feet of soft sand, silt, and clay. Subsidence, or settling of the ground surface, occurs naturally due to the consolidation and oxidation of organic soils (called "marsh" in New Orleans) and local groundwater pumping. In the past, flooding and deposition of sediments from the Mississippi River counterbalanced the natural subsidence, leaving southeast Louisiana at or
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">
          above sea level
         </a>
         . However, due to major flood control structures being built upstream on the Mississippi River and levees being built around New Orleans, fresh layers of sediment are not replenishing the ground lost by subsidence.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ASCE_69-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-ASCE-69">
           [69]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">
         ”
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       In May 2016, NASA published a study
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which suggested that most areas were, in fact, experiencing subsidence at a "highly variable rate" which was "generally consistent with, but somewhat higher than, previous studies."
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">
        Cityscape
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Wards_of_New_Orleans" title="Wards of New Orleans">
        Wards of New Orleans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Neighborhoods_in_New_Orleans" title="Neighborhoods in New Orleans">
        Neighborhoods in New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Orleans.bourbon.arp.750pix.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="563" data-file-width="750" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Orleans.bourbon.arp.750pix.jpg/250px-Orleans.bourbon.arp.750pix.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Orleans.bourbon.arp.750pix.jpg/375px-Orleans.bourbon.arp.750pix.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Orleans.bourbon.arp.750pix.jpg/500px-Orleans.bourbon.arp.750pix.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Orleans.bourbon.arp.750pix.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Street" title="Bourbon Street">
          Bourbon Street
         </a>
         , New Orleans, in 2003, looking towards Canal Street
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colorful_houses_in_New_Orleans.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1167" data-file-width="1297" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Colorful_houses_in_New_Orleans.jpg/250px-Colorful_houses_in_New_Orleans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Colorful_houses_in_New_Orleans.jpg/375px-Colorful_houses_in_New_Orleans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Colorful_houses_in_New_Orleans.jpg/500px-Colorful_houses_in_New_Orleans.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colorful_houses_in_New_Orleans.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         New Orleans contains many distinctive neighborhoods.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Central_Business_District" title="New Orleans Central Business District">
        Central Business District
       </a>
       is located immediately north and west of the Mississippi and was historically called the "American Quarter" or "American Sector." It was developed after the heart of French and Spanish settlement. It includes
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lafayette_Square,_New_Orleans" title="Lafayette Square, New Orleans">
        Lafayette Square
       </a>
       . Most streets in this area fan out from a central point. Major streets include
       <a href="/wiki/Canal_Street,_New_Orleans" title="Canal Street, New Orleans">
        Canal Street
       </a>
       , Poydras Street, Tulane Avenue and Loyola Avenue. Canal Street divides the traditional "
       <a href="/wiki/Downtown_New_Orleans" title="Downtown New Orleans">
        downtown
       </a>
       " area from the "
       <a href="/wiki/Uptown_New_Orleans" title="Uptown New Orleans">
        uptown
       </a>
       " area.
      </p>
      <p>
       Every street crossing Canal Street between the Mississippi River and
       <a href="/wiki/Rampart_Street" title="Rampart Street">
        Rampart Street
       </a>
       , which is the northern edge of the French Quarter, has a different name for the "uptown" and "downtown" portions. For example,
       <a href="/wiki/St._Charles_Avenue" title="St. Charles Avenue">
        St. Charles Avenue
       </a>
       , known for its street car line, is called
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Street,_New_Orleans" title="Royal Street, New Orleans">
        Royal Street
       </a>
       below Canal Street, though where it traverses the Central Business District between Canal and Lee Circle, it is properly called St. Charles Street.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Elsewhere in the city, Canal Street serves as the dividing point between the "South" and "North" portions of various streets. In the local
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/parlance" title="wikt:parlance">
        parlance
       </a>
       <i>
        downtown
       </i>
       means "downriver from Canal Street", while
       <i>
        uptown
       </i>
       means "upriver from Canal Street". Downtown neighborhoods include the
       <a href="/wiki/French_Quarter" title="French Quarter">
        French Quarter
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Trem%C3%A9" title="Tremé">
        Tremé
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/7th_Ward_of_New_Orleans" title="7th Ward of New Orleans">
        7th Ward
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Faubourg_Marigny" title="Faubourg Marigny">
        Faubourg Marigny
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bywater,_New_Orleans" title="Bywater, New Orleans">
        Bywater
       </a>
       (the Upper Ninth Ward), and the Lower
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ninth_Ward_of_New_Orleans" title="Ninth Ward of New Orleans">
        Ninth Ward
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Uptown_New_Orleans" title="Uptown New Orleans">
        Uptown
       </a>
       neighborhoods include the Warehouse District, the
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Garden_District,_New_Orleans" title="Lower Garden District, New Orleans">
        Lower Garden District
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Garden_District,_New_Orleans" title="Garden District, New Orleans">
        Garden District
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Irish_Channel,_New_Orleans" title="Irish Channel, New Orleans">
        Irish Channel
       </a>
       , the University District,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carrollton,_Louisiana" title="Carrollton, Louisiana">
        Carrollton
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gert_Town,_New_Orleans" title="Gert Town, New Orleans">
        Gert Town
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fontainebleau,_New_Orleans" title="Fontainebleau, New Orleans">
        Fontainebleau
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Broadmoor,_New_Orleans" title="Broadmoor, New Orleans">
        Broadmoor
       </a>
       . However, the Warehouse and the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Central_Business_District" title="New Orleans Central Business District">
        Central Business District
       </a>
       are frequently called "Downtown" as a specific region, as in the Downtown Development District.
      </p>
      <p>
       Other major districts within the city include
       <a href="/wiki/Bayou_St._John,_New_Orleans" title="Bayou St. John, New Orleans">
        Bayou St. John
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mid-City_New_Orleans" title="Mid-City New Orleans">
        Mid-City
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gentilly,_New_Orleans" title="Gentilly, New Orleans">
        Gentilly
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lakeview,_New_Orleans" title="Lakeview, New Orleans">
        Lakeview
       </a>
       , Lakefront,
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_New_Orleans" title="Eastern New Orleans">
        New Orleans East
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Algiers,_New_Orleans" title="Algiers, New Orleans">
        Algiers
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_and_residential_architecture">
        Historic and residential architecture
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Buildings_and_architecture_of_New_Orleans" title="Buildings and architecture of New Orleans">
        Buildings and architecture of New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans is world-famous for its abundance of architectural styles that reflect the city's multicultural heritage. Though New Orleans possesses numerous structures of national architectural significance, it is equally, if not more, revered for its enormous, largely intact (even post-Katrina) historic built environment. Twenty National Register Historic Districts have been established, and fourteen local historic districts aid in preservation. Thirteen of the districts are administered by the New Orleans Historic District Landmarks Commission (HDLC), while one—the French Quarter—is administered by the Vieux Carre Commission (VCC). Additionally, both the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">
        National Park Service
       </a>
       , via the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">
        National Register of Historic Places
       </a>
       , and the HDLC have landmarked individual buildings, many of which lie outside the boundaries of existing historic districts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Housing styles include the
       <a href="/wiki/Shotgun_house" title="Shotgun house">
        shotgun house
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Bungalow" title="Bungalow">
        bungalow
       </a>
       style. Creole cottages and townhouses, notable for their large courtyards and intricate iron balconies, line the streets of the French Quarter. American townhouses, double-gallery houses, and Raised Center-Hall Cottages are notable.
       <a href="/wiki/St._Charles_Avenue" title="St. Charles Avenue">
        St. Charles Avenue
       </a>
       is famed for its large
       <a href="/wiki/Antebellum_architecture" title="Antebellum architecture">
        antebellum homes
       </a>
       . Its mansions are in various styles, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Greek_Revival_architecture" title="Greek Revival architecture">
        Greek Revival
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/American_colonial_architecture" title="American colonial architecture">
        American Colonial
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">
        Victorian
       </a>
       styles of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Anne_Style_architecture" title="Queen Anne Style architecture">
        Queen Anne
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Italianate_architecture" title="Italianate architecture">
        Italianate architecture
       </a>
       . New Orleans is also noted for its large, European-style Catholic cemeteries.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tallest_buildings">
        Tallest buildings
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_New_Orleans" title="List of tallest buildings in New Orleans">
        List of tallest buildings in New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:287px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_skyline_2012_from_Danziger.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3136" data-file-width="4735" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/New_Orleans_skyline_2012_from_Danziger.jpg/285px-New_Orleans_skyline_2012_from_Danziger.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/New_Orleans_skyline_2012_from_Danziger.jpg/428px-New_Orleans_skyline_2012_from_Danziger.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/New_Orleans_skyline_2012_from_Danziger.jpg/570px-New_Orleans_skyline_2012_from_Danziger.jpg 2x" width="285"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_skyline_2012_from_Danziger.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Pictured in the New Orleans skyline is
         <a href="/wiki/One_Shell_Square" title="One Shell Square">
          One Shell Square
         </a>
         (towards left), New Orleans' tallest building, standing at 697 ft (212 m)) as well as
         <a href="/wiki/Place_St._Charles" title="Place St. Charles">
          Place St. Charles
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Tower" title="Plaza Tower">
          Plaza Tower
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/First_Bank_and_Trust_Tower" title="First Bank and Trust Tower">
          First Bank and Trust Tower
         </a>
         , and
         <a href="/wiki/Energy_Centre" title="Energy Centre">
          Energy Centre
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       For much of its history, New Orleans' skyline displayed only low- and mid- rise structures. The soft soils are susceptible to subsidence, and there was doubt about the feasibility of constructing high rises. Developments in engineering throughout the twentieth century eventually made it possible to build sturdy foundations to underlie high rises. In the 1960s, the
       <a href="/wiki/2_Canal_Street" title="2 Canal Street">
        World Trade Center New Orleans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Tower" title="Plaza Tower">
        Plaza Tower
       </a>
       demonstrated skyscrapers' viability.
       <a href="/wiki/One_Shell_Square" title="One Shell Square">
        One Shell Square
       </a>
       became the city's tallest building in 1972. The oil boom of the 1970s and early 1980s redefined New Orleans' skyline with the development of the Poydras Street corridor. Most are clustered along
       <a href="/wiki/Canal_Street,_New_Orleans" title="Canal Street, New Orleans">
        Canal Street
       </a>
       and Poydras Street in the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Central_Business_District" title="New Orleans Central Business District">
        Central Business District
       </a>
       .
      </p>

         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS_New_Orleans/Baton_Rouge,_LA_(LIX)_77-1">

         </sup>
        </td>

      </table>
      <p>
       The climate is
       <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">
        humid subtropical
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen climate classification
       </a>
       <i>
        Cfa
       </i>
       ), with short, generally mild winters and hot, humid summers; most suburbs and parts of Wards 9 and 15 fall in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USDA" title="USDA">
        USDA
       </a>
       Plant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hardiness_Zone" title="Hardiness Zone">
        Hardiness Zone
       </a>
       9a, while the city's other 15 wards are rated 9b in whole.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The monthly daily average temperature ranges from 53.4 °F (11.9 °C) in January to 83.3 °F (28.5 °C) in July and August. Officially, as measured at New Orleans International Airport, temperature records range from 11 to 102 °F (−12 to 39 °C) on December 23, 1989 and August 22, 1980, respectively; Audubon Park has recorded temperatures ranging from 6 °F (−14 °C) on
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Blizzard_of_1899" title="Great Blizzard of 1899">
        February 13, 1899
       </a>
       up to 104 °F (40 °C) on June 24, 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS_New_Orleans/Baton_Rouge,_LA_(LIX)_77-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-NWS_New_Orleans/Baton_Rouge,_LA_(LIX)-77">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Dewpoints in the summer months (June–August) are relatively high, ranging from 71.1 to 73.4 °F (21.7 to 23.0 °C).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMO_1961–90_KMSY_79-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-WMO_1961–90_KMSY-79">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Snow_in_New_Orleans_by_evreniz.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="519" data-file-width="800" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Snow_in_New_Orleans_by_evreniz.jpg/250px-Snow_in_New_Orleans_by_evreniz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Snow_in_New_Orleans_by_evreniz.jpg/375px-Snow_in_New_Orleans_by_evreniz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Snow_in_New_Orleans_by_evreniz.jpg/500px-Snow_in_New_Orleans_by_evreniz.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Snow_in_New_Orleans_by_evreniz.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Snow falls on
         <a href="/wiki/St._Charles_Avenue" title="St. Charles Avenue">
          St. Charles Avenue
         </a>
         in December 2008.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The average precipitation is 62.5 inches (1,590 mm) annually; the summer months are the wettest, while October is the driest month.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS_New_Orleans/Baton_Rouge,_LA_(LIX)_77-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-NWS_New_Orleans/Baton_Rouge,_LA_(LIX)-77">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Precipitation in winter usually accompanies the passing of a cold front. On average, there are 77 days of 90 °F (32 °C)+ highs, 8.1 days per winter where the high does not exceed 50 °F (10 °C), and 8.0 nights with freezing lows annually. It is rare for the temperature to reach 20 or 100 °F (−7 or 38 °C), with the last occurrence of each being February 5, 1996 and June 26, 2016, respectively.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS_New_Orleans/Baton_Rouge,_LA_(LIX)_77-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-NWS_New_Orleans/Baton_Rouge,_LA_(LIX)-77">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans experiences snowfall only on rare occasions. A small amount of snow fell during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_Christmas_Eve_Snowstorm" title="2004 Christmas Eve Snowstorm">
        2004 Christmas Eve Snowstorm
       </a>
       and again on
       <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">
        Christmas
       </a>
       (December 25) when a combination of rain, sleet, and snow fell on the city, leaving some bridges icy. The
       <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve_1963_snowstorm" title="New Year's Eve 1963 snowstorm">
        New Year's Eve 1963 snowstorm
       </a>
       affected New Orleans and brought 4.5 inches (11 cm). Snow fell again on December 22, 1989, when most of the city received 1–2 inches (2.5–5.1 cm).
      </p>
      <p>
       The last significant snowfall in New Orleans was on the morning of December 11, 2008.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Threat_from_tropical_cyclones">
        Threat from tropical cyclones
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricanes_Category_3_or_greater_within_100_miles_of_New_Orleans.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="734" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Hurricanes_Category_3_or_greater_within_100_miles_of_New_Orleans.jpg/250px-Hurricanes_Category_3_or_greater_within_100_miles_of_New_Orleans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Hurricanes_Category_3_or_greater_within_100_miles_of_New_Orleans.jpg/375px-Hurricanes_Category_3_or_greater_within_100_miles_of_New_Orleans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Hurricanes_Category_3_or_greater_within_100_miles_of_New_Orleans.jpg/500px-Hurricanes_Category_3_or_greater_within_100_miles_of_New_Orleans.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricanes_Category_3_or_greater_within_100_miles_of_New_Orleans.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Hurricanes of Category 3 or greater passing within 100 miles 1852–2005 (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOAA" title="NOAA">
          NOAA
         </a>
         )
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">
        Hurricanes
       </a>
       pose a severe threat to the area, and the city is particularly at risk because of its low elevation, because it is surrounded by water from the north, east, and south and because of Louisiana's sinking coast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Katrina_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Katrina-81">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">
        Federal Emergency Management Agency
       </a>
       , New Orleans is the nation's most vulnerable city to hurricanes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Indeed, portions of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_metropolitan_area" title="New Orleans metropolitan area">
        Greater New Orleans
       </a>
       have been flooded by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Isle_Hurricane_of_1909" title="Grand Isle Hurricane of 1909">
        Grand Isle Hurricane of 1909
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_83-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-83">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Hurricane_of_1915" title="New Orleans Hurricane of 1915">
        New Orleans Hurricane of 1915
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_83-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-83">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1947_Fort_Lauderdale_Hurricane" title="1947 Fort Lauderdale Hurricane">
        1947 Fort Lauderdale Hurricane
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_83-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-83">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Flossy" title="Hurricane Flossy">
        Hurricane Flossy
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in 1956,
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Betsy" title="Hurricane Betsy">
        Hurricane Betsy
       </a>
       in 1965,
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Georges" title="Hurricane Georges">
        Hurricane Georges
       </a>
       in 1998, Hurricanes
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">
        Katrina
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Rita" title="Hurricane Rita">
        Rita
       </a>
       in 2005, and
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gustav" title="Hurricane Gustav">
        Hurricane Gustav
       </a>
       in 2008, with the flooding in Betsy being significant and in a few neighborhoods severe, and that in Katrina being disastrous in the majority of the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2005, storm surge from Hurricane Katrina caused catastrophic failure of the
       <a href="/wiki/Flood_Control_Act_of_1965" title="Flood Control Act of 1965">
        federally designed and built
       </a>
       levees, flooding 80% of the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A report by the American Society of Civil Engineers says that "had the levees and floodwalls not failed and had the pump stations operated, nearly two-thirds of the deaths would not have occurred".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ASCE_69-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ASCE-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans has always had to consider the risk of hurricanes, but the risks are dramatically greater today due to coastal erosion from human interference.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barry_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-barry-90">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since the beginning of the 20th century, it has been estimated that Louisiana has lost 2,000 square miles (5,000 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ) of coast (including many of its barrier islands), which once protected New Orleans against storm surge. Following Hurricane Katrina, the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">
        Army Corps of Engineers
       </a>
       has instituted massive levee repair and hurricane protection measures to protect the city.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2006, Louisiana voters overwhelmingly adopted an amendment to the state's constitution to dedicate all revenues from off-shore drilling to restore Louisiana's eroding coast line.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Congress has allocated $7 billion to bolster New Orleans' flood protection.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to a study by the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">
        National Academy of Engineering
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council" title="United States National Research Council">
        National Research Council
       </a>
       , levees and floodwalls surrounding New Orleans—no matter how large or sturdy—cannot provide absolute protection against overtopping or failure in extreme events. Levees and floodwalls should be viewed as a way to reduce risks from hurricanes and storm surges, not as measures that completely eliminate risk. For structures in hazardous areas and residents who do not relocate, the committee recommended major floodproofing measures—such as elevating the first floor of buildings to at least the 100-year flood level.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

          <br/>
          1990–2000
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
           <a href="#cite_note-99">
            [96]
           </a>
          </sup>
          2010–2013
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QF_7-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-QF-7">
            [7]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </div>
         <br/>
         Source:
         <center>
          U.S. Decennial Census
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DecennialCensus_100-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-DecennialCensus-100">
            [97]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </center>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">
        2010 Census
       </a>
       , 343,829 people and 189,896 households lived in New Orleans. Its racial and ethnic makeup was 60.2%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">
        African American
       </a>
       , 33.0%
       <a href="/wiki/White_Americans" title="White Americans">
        White
       </a>
       , 2.9%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">
        Asian
       </a>
       (1.7% Vietnamese, 0.3% Indian, 0.3% Chinese, 0.1% Filipino, 0.1% Korean), 0.0%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" title="Pacific Islander American">
        Pacific Islander
       </a>
       , and 1.7% were people of
       <a href="/wiki/Multiracial_Americans" title="Multiracial Americans">
        two or more races
       </a>
       . People of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_American" title="Hispanic and Latino American">
        Hispanic or Latino
       </a>
       origin made up 5.3% of the population; 1.3% is Mexican, 1.3% Honduran, 0.4% Cuban, 0.3% Puerto Rican, and 0.3% Nicaraguan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_New_Orleans_(5560463750).png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3009" data-file-width="3009" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_New_Orleans_%285560463750%29.png/220px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_New_Orleans_%285560463750%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_New_Orleans_%285560463750%29.png/330px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_New_Orleans_%285560463750%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_New_Orleans_%285560463750%29.png/440px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_New_Orleans_%285560463750%29.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_New_Orleans_(5560463750).png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of racial distribution in New Orleans, 2010 U.S. Census. Each dot is 25 people:
         <span style="color:#ff0000">
          <b>
           White
          </b>
         </span>
         ,
         <span style="color:#0000ff">
          <b>
           Black
          </b>
         </span>
         ,
         <span style="color:#00ff80">
          <b>
           Asian
          </b>
         </span>
         ,
         <span style="color:#ff8000">
          <b>
           Hispanic
          </b>
         </span>
         , or
         <b>
          Other
         </b>
         (yellow)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The last population estimate before Hurricane Katrina was 454,865, as of July 1, 2005.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A population analysis released in August 2007 estimated the population to be 273,000, 60% of the pre-Katrina population and an increase of about 50,000 since July 2006.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A September 2007 report by The Greater New Orleans Community Data Center, which tracks population based on U.S. Postal Service figures, found that in August 2007, just over 137,000 households received mail. That compares with about 198,000 households in July 2005, representing about 70% of pre-Katrina population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       More recently, the Census Bureau revised upward its 2008 population estimate for the city, to 336,644 inhabitants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Orleans_2010_57-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-New_Orleans_2010-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2010, estimates showed that neighborhoods that did not flood were near or even greater than 100% of their pre-Katrina populations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_58-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A 2006 study by researchers at
       <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">
        Tulane University
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">
        University of California, Berkeley
       </a>
       determined that as many as 10,000 to 14,000
       <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration" title="Illegal immigration">
        undocumented immigrants
       </a>
       , many from
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       , resided in New Orleans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-undoc_105-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-undoc-105">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Janet_Murgu%C3%ADa" title="Janet Murguía">
        Janet Murguía
       </a>
       , president and chief executive officer of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Council_of_La_Raza" title="National Council of La Raza">
        National Council of La Raza
       </a>
       , stated that up to 120,000 Hispanic workers lived in New Orleans. In June 2007, one study stated that the Hispanic population had risen from 15,000, pre-Katrina, to over 50,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable collapsible" style="font-size: 90%;">
