      <p>
       As of 2010
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_Orleans&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , 90.31% of residents age 5 and older spoke English at home as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_language" title="Primary language">
        primary language
       </a>
       , while 4.84% spoke Spanish, 1.87% Vietnamese, and 1.05% spoke French. In total, 9.69% population age 5 and older spoke a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_language" title="Mother language">
        mother language
       </a>
       other than English.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       New Orleans' colonial history of French and Spanish settlement generated a strong
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
        Roman Catholic
       </a>
       tradition. Catholic missions ministered to slaves and free people of color and established schools for them. In addition, many late 19th and early 20th century European immigrants, such as the Irish, some Germans, and Italians were Catholic. Within the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_New_Orleans" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of New Orleans">
        Archdiocese
       </a>
       (which includes not only the city but the surrounding Parishes as well), 35.9% percent of the population is Roman Catholic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Catholicism is reflected in French and Spanish cultural traditions, including its many parochial schools, street names, architecture and festivals, including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Mardi_Gras" title="New Orleans Mardi Gras">
        Mardi Gras
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stlouiscathedralnight.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2e/Stlouiscathedralnight.jpg/300px-Stlouiscathedralnight.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2e/Stlouiscathedralnight.jpg/450px-Stlouiscathedralnight.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2e/Stlouiscathedralnight.jpg/600px-Stlouiscathedralnight.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stlouiscathedralnight.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cathedral,_New_Orleans" title="St. Louis Cathedral, New Orleans">
          Cathedral-Basilica of St. Louis, King of France
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans displays a distinctive variety of
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Voodoo" title="Louisiana Voodoo">
        Louisiana Voodoo
       </a>
       , due in part to
       <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">
        syncretism
       </a>
       with African and Afro-Caribbean Roman Catholic beliefs. The fame of voodoo practitioner
       <a href="/wiki/Marie_Laveau" title="Marie Laveau">
        Marie Laveau
       </a>
       contributed to this, as did New Orleans' Caribbean cultural influences.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BostonGlobeNorthernmost_114-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BostonGlobeNorthernmost-114">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although the tourism industry strongly associated Voodoo with the city, only a small number of people are serious adherents.
      </p>
      <p>
       Jewish settlers, primarily
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardim" title="Sephardim">
        Sephardim
       </a>
       , settled in New Orleans from the early nineteenth century. Some migrated from the communities established in the colonial years in
       <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">
        Charleston, South Carolina
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">
        Savannah, Georgia
       </a>
       . The merchant
       <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Cohen_Labatt" title="Abraham Cohen Labatt">
        Abraham Cohen Labatt
       </a>
       helped found the first Jewish congregation in New Orleans in the 1830s, which became known as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardic_Jews" title="Sephardic Jews">
        Portuguese Jewish
       </a>
       Nefutzot Yehudah congregation (he and some other members were
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardic_Jews" title="Sephardic Jews">
        Sephardic Jews
       </a>
       , whose ancestors had lived in Portugal and Spain).
       <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">
        Ashkenazi Jews
       </a>
       from eastern Europe immigrated in the late 19th and 20th centuries. By the 21st century, 10,000
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jew" title="Jew">
        Jews
       </a>
       lived in New Orleans. This number dropped to 7,000 after Hurricane Katrina. New Orleans synagogues lost members, but most re-opened in their original locations. The exception was
       <a href="/wiki/Congregation_Beth_Israel_(New_Orleans)" title="Congregation Beth Israel (New Orleans)">
        Congregation Beth Israel
       </a>
       , the oldest and most prominent
       <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Judaism" title="Orthodox Judaism">
        Orthodox
       </a>
       synagogue in the New Orleans region. Beth Israel's building in Lakeview was destroyed by flooding. After seven years of holding services in temporary quarters, the congregation consecrated a new synagogue on land purchased from the
       <a href="/wiki/Reform_Judaism" title="Reform Judaism">
        Reform
       </a>
       Congregation Gates of Prayer in
       <a href="/wiki/Metairie,_Louisiana" title="Metairie, Louisiana">
        Metairie
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beth_Israel_7_years_115-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Beth_Israel_7_years-115">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">
        Ethnic groups
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Hondurans_in_New_Orleans" title="Hondurans in New Orleans">
        Hondurans in New Orleans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Italians_in_New_Orleans" title="Italians in New Orleans">
        Italians in New Orleans
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_in_New_Orleans" title="Vietnamese in New Orleans">
        Vietnamese in New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       As of 2011
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_Orleans&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the Hispanic population had grown in the New Orleans area, including in
       <a href="/wiki/Kenner,_Louisiana" title="Kenner, Louisiana">
        Kenner
       </a>
       , central
       <a href="/wiki/Metairie,_Louisiana" title="Metairie, Louisiana">
        Metairie
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Terrytown,_Louisiana" title="Terrytown, Louisiana">
        Terrytown
       </a>
       in Jefferson Parish and
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_New_Orleans" title="Eastern New Orleans">
        eastern New Orleans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mid-City_New_Orleans" title="Mid-City New Orleans">
        Mid-City
       </a>
       in New Orleans proper.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HispboomKENNER_116-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HispboomKENNER-116">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After Katrina the small
       <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Americans" title="Brazilian Americans">
        Brazilian-American
       </a>
       population expanded. Portuguese speakers were the second most numerous group to take
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_as_a_second_language" title="English as a second language">
        English as a second language
       </a>
       classes in the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_New_Orleans" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of New Orleans">
        Roman Catholic Archdiocese
       </a>
       , after Spanish speakers. Many Brazilians worked in skilled trades such as tile and flooring, although fewer worked as day laborers than did Latinos. Many had moved from Brazilian communities in the
       <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">
        Northeastern United States
       </a>
       , Florida and Georgia. Brazilians settled throughout the metropolitan area. Most were undocumented. In January 2008 the New Orleans Brazilian population had a mid-range estimate of 3,000. By 2008 Brazilians had opened many small churches, shops and restaurants catering to their community.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Changes_in_population">
        Changes in population
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Beginning in 1960, the population decreased
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hollander_2008_118-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hollander_2008-118">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frey_1987_119-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Frey_1987-119">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       due to factors such as the cycles of oil production and tourism, and as
       <a href="/wiki/Suburbanization" title="Suburbanization">
        suburbanization
       </a>
       increased (as with many cities),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fussell_2007_120-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Fussell_2007-120">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and jobs migrated to surrounding parishes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Katz_2006_121-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Katz_2006-121">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This economic and population decline resulted in high levels of poverty in the city; in 1960 it had the fifth-highest poverty rate of all US cities,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spain_1979_122-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Spain_1979-122">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and was almost twice the national average in 2005, at 24.5%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fussell_2007_120-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Fussell_2007-120">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       New Orleans experienced an increase in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Residential_segregation" title="Residential segregation">
        residential segregation
       </a>
       from 1900 to 1980, leaving the disproportionately African-American poor
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Katz_2006_121-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Katz_2006-121">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in older, low-lying locations. These areas were especially susceptible to flood and storm damage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kates_2006_123-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kates_2006-123">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Katrina displaced 800,000 people, contributing significantly to the decline.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nelson_2011_124-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nelson_2011-124">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       African Americans, renters, the elderly, and people with low income were disproportionately affected by Katrina, compared to affluent and white residents.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nelson_2007_125-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nelson_2007-125">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morse_2008_126-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Morse_2008-126">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In Katrina's aftermath, city government commissioned groups such as
       <a href="/wiki/Bring_New_Orleans_Back_Commission" title="Bring New Orleans Back Commission">
        Bring New Orleans Back Commission
       </a>
       , the New Orleans Neighborhood Rebuilding Plan, the Unified New Orleans Plan, and the Office of Recovery Management to contribute to plans addressing depopulation. Their ideas included shrinking the city's
       <a href="/wiki/Footprint" title="Footprint">
        footprint
       </a>
       from before the storm, incorporating community voices into development plans, and creating
       <a href="/wiki/Urban_open_space" title="Urban open space">
        green spaces
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nelson_2007_125-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nelson_2007-125">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
       some of which incited controversy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olshanski_2008_127-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Olshanski_2008-127">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reardon_2008_128-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Reardon_2008-128">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From 2010 to 2014 the city grew by 12%, adding an average of more than 10,000 new residents each year following the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">
        2010 Census
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014CensusEst_94-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-2014CensusEst-94">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tanker_IVER_SPRING_on_Mississippi_River_in_New_Orleans.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Tanker_IVER_SPRING_on_Mississippi_River_in_New_Orleans.jpeg/220px-Tanker_IVER_SPRING_on_Mississippi_River_in_New_Orleans.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Tanker_IVER_SPRING_on_Mississippi_River_in_New_Orleans.jpeg/330px-Tanker_IVER_SPRING_on_Mississippi_River_in_New_Orleans.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Tanker_IVER_SPRING_on_Mississippi_River_in_New_Orleans.jpeg/440px-Tanker_IVER_SPRING_on_Mississippi_River_in_New_Orleans.jpeg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tanker_IVER_SPRING_on_Mississippi_River_in_New_Orleans.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tank_ship" title="Tank ship">
          tanker
         </a>
         on the Mississippi River in New Orleans
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Intracoastal_Waterway_Louisiana.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Intracoastal_Waterway_Louisiana.jpg/220px-Intracoastal_Waterway_Louisiana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Intracoastal_Waterway_Louisiana.jpg/330px-Intracoastal_Waterway_Louisiana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Intracoastal_Waterway_Louisiana.jpg/440px-Intracoastal_Waterway_Louisiana.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Intracoastal_Waterway_Louisiana.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Intracoastal_Waterway" title="Intracoastal Waterway">
          Intracoastal Waterway
         </a>
         near New Orleans
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans operates
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_New_Orleans" title="Port of New Orleans">
        one of the world's largest and busiest ports
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_metropolitan_area" title="New Orleans metropolitan area">
        metropolitan New Orleans
       </a>
       is a center of maritime industry. The region accounts for a significant portion of the nation's
       <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">
        oil refining
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">
        petrochemical production
       </a>
       , and serves as a
       <a href="/wiki/White-collar_worker" title="White-collar worker">
        white-collar
       </a>
       corporate base for onshore and offshore
       <a href="/wiki/Extraction_of_petroleum" title="Extraction of petroleum">
        petroleum
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">
        natural gas
       </a>
       production.
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans is also a center for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Higher_learning" title="Higher learning">
        higher learning
       </a>
       , with over 50,000 students enrolled in the region's eleven two- and four-year degree-granting institutions.
       <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">
        Tulane University
       </a>
       , a top-50 research university, is located in
       <a href="/wiki/Uptown_New_Orleans" title="Uptown New Orleans">
        Uptown
       </a>
       . Metropolitan New Orleans is a major regional hub for the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_care_industry" title="Health care industry">
        health care industry
       </a>
       and boasts a small, globally competitive manufacturing sector. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_central_business_district" title="New Orleans central business district">
        center city
       </a>
       possesses a rapidly growing, entrepreneurial
       <a href="/wiki/Creative_industries" title="Creative industries">
        creative industries
       </a>
       sector and is renowned for its
       <a href="/wiki/Cultural_tourism" title="Cultural tourism">
        cultural tourism
       </a>
       . Greater New Orleans, Inc. (GNO, Inc.)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
        <a href="#cite_note-129">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       acts as the first point-of-contact for regional economic development, coordinating between Louisiana's Department of Economic Development and the various business development agencies.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Port_2">
        Port
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       New Orleans began as a strategically-located trading
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Entrep%C3%B4t" title="Entrepôt">
         entrepôt
        </a>
       </i>
       and it remains, above all, a crucial transportation hub and distribution center for waterborne commerce. The
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_New_Orleans" title="Port of New Orleans">
        Port
       </a>
       is the fifth-largest in the United States based on cargo volume and second-largest in the state after the
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_South_Louisiana" title="Port of South Louisiana">
        Port of South Louisiana
       </a>
       . It is the twelfth-largest in the U.S. based on cargo value. The Port of South Louisiana, also located in the New Orleans area, is the world's busiest in terms of bulk tonnage. When combined with Port of New Orleans, it forms the 4th-largest port system in volume. Many shipbuilding, shipping, logistics, freight forwarding and commodity brokerage firms either are based in metropolitan New Orleans or maintain a local presence. Examples include Intermarine, Bisso Towboat,
       <a href="/wiki/Northrop_Grumman_Ship_Systems" title="Northrop Grumman Ship Systems">
        Northrop Grumman Ship Systems
       </a>
       , Trinity Yachts,
       <a href="/wiki/Expeditors_International" title="Expeditors International">
        Expeditors International
       </a>
       , Bollinger Shipyards, IMTT, International Coffee Corp, Boasso America, Transoceanic Shipping, Transportation Consultants Inc., Dupuy Storage &amp; Forwarding and Silocaf. The largest coffee-roasting plant in the world, operated by
       <a href="/wiki/Folgers" title="Folgers">
        Folgers
       </a>
       , is located in
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_New_Orleans" title="Eastern New Orleans">
        New Orleans East
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans is located near to the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">
        Gulf of Mexico
       </a>
       and its many oil rigs. Louisiana ranks fifth among states in oil production and eighth in
       <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">
        reserves
       </a>
       . It has two of the four
       <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Petroleum_Reserve_(United_States)" title="Strategic Petroleum Reserve (United States)">
        Strategic Petroleum Reserve
       </a>
       (SPR) storage facilities: West Hackberry in
       <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Cameron Parish, Louisiana">
        Cameron Parish
       </a>
       and Bayou Choctaw in
       <a href="/wiki/Iberville_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Iberville Parish, Louisiana">
        Iberville Parish
       </a>
       . The area hosts 17 petroleum refineries, with a combined crude oil distillation capacity of nearly 2.8 million barrels per day (450,000 m
       <sup>
        3
       </sup>
       /d), the second highest after Texas. Louisiana's numerous ports include the
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Offshore_Oil_Port" title="Louisiana Offshore Oil Port">
        Louisiana Offshore Oil Port
       </a>
       (LOOP), which is capable of receiving the largest oil tankers. Given the quantity of oil imports, Louisiana is home to many major pipelines:
       <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">
        Crude Oil
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Exxon" title="Exxon">
        Exxon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">
        Chevron
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">
        BP
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Texaco" title="Texaco">
        Texaco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Shell_Oil_Company" title="Shell Oil Company">
        Shell
       </a>
       , Scurloch-Permian, Mid-Valley, Calumet,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conoco_Inc." title="Conoco Inc.">
        Conoco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Koch_Industries" title="Koch Industries">
        Koch Industries
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Unocal_Corporation" title="Unocal Corporation">
        Unocal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">
        U.S. Dept. of Energy
       </a>
       , Locap); Product (
       <a href="/wiki/TEPPCO_Partners" title="TEPPCO Partners">
        TEPPCO Partners
       </a>
       , Colonial, Plantation, Explorer, Texaco, Collins); and
       <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_petroleum_gas" title="Liquefied petroleum gas">
        Liquefied Petroleum Gas
       </a>
       (Dixie, TEPPCO, Black Lake, Koch, Chevron,
       <a href="/wiki/Dynegy" title="Dynegy">
        Dynegy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kinder_Morgan_Energy_Partners" title="Kinder Morgan Energy Partners">
        Kinder Morgan Energy Partners
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dow_Chemical_Company" title="Dow Chemical Company">
        Dow Chemical Company
       </a>
       , Bridgeline, FMP, Tejas, Texaco, UTP).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
        <a href="#cite_note-130">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Several energy companies have regional headquarters in the area, including
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">
        Royal Dutch Shell
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eni" title="Eni">
        Eni
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">
        Chevron
       </a>
       . Other energy producers and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oilfield_services" title="Oilfield services">
        oilfield services companies
       </a>
       are headquartered in the city or region, and the sector supports a large professional services base of specialized engineering and design firms, as well as a term office for the federal government's
       <a href="/wiki/Minerals_Management_Service" title="Minerals Management Service">
        Minerals Management Service
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Business">
        Business
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">

      <p>
       The city is the home to a single
       <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">
        Fortune 500
       </a>
       company:
       <a href="/wiki/Entergy" title="Entergy">
        Entergy
       </a>
       , a power generation utility and
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant" title="Nuclear power plant">
        nuclear power plant
       </a>
       operations specialist. After Katrina, the city lost its other Fortune 500 company,
       <a href="/wiki/Freeport-McMoRan" title="Freeport-McMoRan">
        Freeport-McMoRan
       </a>
       , when it merged its copper and gold exploration unit with an Arizona company and relocated that division to
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">
        Phoenix
       </a>
       . Its McMoRan Exploration affiliate remains headquartered in New Orleans. Other companies either headquartered or with significant operations in New Orleans include: Pan American Life Insurance, Pool Corp,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_plc" title="Rolls-Royce plc">
        Rolls-Royce
       </a>
       , Newpark Resources,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AT%26T_Inc." title="AT&amp;T Inc.">
        AT&amp;T
       </a>
       , TurboSquid, iSeatz,
       <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">
        IBM
       </a>
       , Navtech,
       <a href="/wiki/Superior_Energy_Services" title="Superior Energy Services">
        Superior Energy Services
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Textron_Marine_%26_Land_Systems" title="Textron Marine &amp; Land Systems">
        Textron Marine &amp; Land Systems
       </a>
       , McDermott International, Pellerin Milnor,
       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">
        Lockheed Martin
       </a>
       , Imperial Trading, Laitram,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harrah%27s_Entertainment" title="Harrah's Entertainment">
        Harrah's Entertainment
       </a>
       , Stewart Enterprises, Edison Chouest Offshore,
       <a href="/wiki/Zatarain%27s" title="Zatarain's">
        Zatarain's
       </a>
       , Waldemar S. Nelson &amp; Co.,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whitney_National_Bank" title="Whitney National Bank">
        Whitney National Bank
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Capital_One" title="Capital One">
        Capital One
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tidewater_(marine_services)" title="Tidewater (marine services)">
        Tidewater Marine
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Popeyes_Chicken_%26_Biscuits" title="Popeyes Chicken &amp; Biscuits">
        Popeyes Chicken &amp; Biscuits
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Parsons_Brinckerhoff" title="Parsons Brinckerhoff">
        Parsons Brinckerhoff
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/MWH_Global" title="MWH Global">
        MWH Global
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CH2M_HILL" title="CH2M HILL">
        CH2M HILL
       </a>
       , Energy Partners Ltd, The Receivables Exchange,
       <a href="/wiki/GE_Capital" title="GE Capital">
        GE Capital
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Smoothie_King" title="Smoothie King">
        Smoothie King
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourist_and_convention_business">
        Tourist and convention business
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Tourism is another staple of the city's economy. Perhaps more visible than any other sector, New Orleans' tourist and convention industry is a $5.5 billion industry that accounts for 40 percent of city tax revenues. In 2004, the hospitality industry employed 85,000 people, making it the city's top economic sector as measured by employment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-0607marketing_131-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-0607marketing-131">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       New Orleans also hosts the World Cultural Economic Forum (WCEF). The forum, held annually at the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Morial_Convention_Center" title="New Orleans Morial Convention Center">
        New Orleans Morial Convention Center
       </a>
       , is directed toward promoting cultural and economic development opportunities through the strategic convening of cultural ambassadors and leaders from around the world. The first WCEF took place in October 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
        <a href="#cite_note-132">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other">
        Other
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Federal agencies and the Armed forces operate significant facilities there. The
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Fifth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Fifth Circuit">
        U.S. Fifth Circuit Court of Appeals
       </a>
       operates at the US Courthouse downtown.
       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
        NASA
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Michoud_Assembly_Facility" title="Michoud Assembly Facility">
        Michoud rocket factory
       </a>
       is located in
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_New_Orleans" title="Eastern New Orleans">
        New Orleans East
       </a>
       and is operated by
       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">
        Lockheed Martin
       </a>
       . It is a huge manufacturing facility that produced the external fuel tanks for the
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">
        Space Shuttles
       </a>
       and is now used for the construction of NASA's Space Launch System. The rocket factory lies within the enormous New Orleans Regional Business Park, also home to the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Finance_Center" title="National Finance Center">
        National Finance Center
       </a>
       , operated by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">
        United States Department of Agriculture
       </a>
       (USDA), and the Crescent Crown distribution center. Other large governmental installations include the U.S. Navy's
       <a href="/wiki/Space_and_Naval_Warfare_Systems_Command" title="Space and Naval Warfare Systems Command">
        Space and Naval Warfare (SPAWAR) Systems Command
       </a>
       , located within the University of New Orleans Research and Technology Park in
       <a href="/wiki/Gentilly,_New_Orleans" title="Gentilly, New Orleans">
        Gentilly
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Joint_Reserve_Base_New_Orleans" title="Naval Air Station Joint Reserve Base New Orleans">
        Naval Air Station Joint Reserve Base New Orleans
       </a>
       ; and the headquarters for the Marine Force Reserves in Federal City in
       <a href="/wiki/Algiers,_New_Orleans" title="Algiers, New Orleans">
        Algiers
       </a>
       .
      </p>

       </tr>
      </table>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_contemporary_life">
        Culture and contemporary life
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_New_Orleans" title="Culture of New Orleans">
        Culture of New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_New_Orleans#Museums_and_other_attractions" title="Culture of New Orleans">
        Culture of New Orleans § Museums and other attractions
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            verification
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_Orleans&amp;action=edit">

           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (May 2013)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>

            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       New Orleans has many visitor attractions, from the world-renowned
       <a href="/wiki/French_Quarter" title="French Quarter">
        French Quarter
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/St._Charles_Avenue" title="St. Charles Avenue">
        St. Charles Avenue
       </a>
       , (home of
       <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">
        Tulane
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Loyola_University_New_Orleans" title="Loyola University New Orleans">
        Loyola
       </a>
       Universities, the historic
       <a href="/wiki/Pontchartrain_Hotel" title="Pontchartrain Hotel">
        Pontchartrain Hotel
       </a>
       and many 19th-century mansions) to
       <a href="/wiki/Magazine_Street" title="Magazine Street">
        Magazine Street
       </a>
       with its boutique stores and antique shops.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Altaner.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Altaner.jpg/235px-Altaner.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Altaner.jpg/353px-Altaner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Altaner.jpg/470px-Altaner.jpg 2x" width="235"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Altaner.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/French_Quarter" title="French Quarter">
          French Quarter
         </a>
         (2002)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New-Orleans-Street-Artist-1988-205.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="4608" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/New-Orleans-Street-Artist-1988-205.jpg/235px-New-Orleans-Street-Artist-1988-205.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/New-Orleans-Street-Artist-1988-205.jpg/353px-New-Orleans-Street-Artist-1988-205.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/New-Orleans-Street-Artist-1988-205.jpg/470px-New-Orleans-Street-Artist-1988-205.jpg 2x" width="235"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New-Orleans-Street-Artist-1988-205.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Street_artist" title="Street artist">
          Street artist
         </a>
         in the French Quarter (1988)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to current travel guides, New Orleans is one of the top ten most-visited cities in the United States; 10.1 million visitors came to New Orleans in 2004.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-0607marketing_131-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-0607marketing-131">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
        <a href="#cite_note-134">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Prior to Katrina, 265 hotels with 38,338 rooms operated in the Greater New Orleans Area. In May 2007, that had declined to some 140 hotels and motels with over 31,000 rooms.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Orleans'_Recovery_as_of_May_2007_135-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-New_Orleans'_Recovery_as_of_May_2007-135">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A 2009
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Travel_%2B_Leisure" title="Travel + Leisure">
         Travel + Leisure
        </a>
       </i>
       poll of "America's Favorite Cities" ranked New Orleans first in ten categories, the most first-place rankings of the 30 cities included. According to the poll, New Orleans was the best U.S. city as a spring break destination and for "wild weekends", stylish boutique hotels, cocktail hours, singles/bar scenes, live music/concerts and bands, antique and vintage shops, cafés/coffee bars, neighborhood restaurants, and
       <a href="/wiki/People_watching" title="People watching">
        people watching
       </a>
       . The city ranked second for: friendliness (behind
       <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">
        Charleston, South Carolina
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Gay" title="Gay">
        gay
       </a>
       -friendliness (behind San Francisco),
       <a href="/wiki/Bed_and_breakfast" title="Bed and breakfast">
        bed and breakfast
       </a>
       hotels/inns, and ethnic food. However, the city placed near the bottom in cleanliness, safety and as a family destination.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
        <a href="#cite_note-136">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
        <a href="#cite_note-137">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The French Quarter (known locally as "the Quarter" or
       <i>
        Vieux Carré
       </i>
       ), which was the colonial-era city and is bounded by the Mississippi River,
       <a href="/wiki/Rampart_Street" title="Rampart Street">
        Rampart Street
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Canal_Street,_New_Orleans" title="Canal Street, New Orleans">
        Canal Street
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Esplanade_Avenue,_New_Orleans" title="Esplanade Avenue, New Orleans">
        Esplanade Avenue
       </a>
       , contains popular hotels, bars and nightclubs. Notable tourist attractions in the Quarter include
       <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Street" title="Bourbon Street">
        Bourbon Street
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Square_(New_Orleans)" title="Jackson Square (New Orleans)">
        Jackson Square
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cathedral_(New_Orleans)" title="St. Louis Cathedral (New Orleans)">
        St. Louis Cathedral
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/French_Market" title="French Market">
        French Market
       </a>
       (including
       <a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_du_Monde" title="Café du Monde">
        Café du Monde
       </a>
       , famous for
       <a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_au_lait" title="Café au lait">
        café au lait
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Beignet" title="Beignet">
        beignets
       </a>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Preservation_Hall" title="Preservation Hall">
        Preservation Hall
       </a>
       . Also in the French Quarter is the old
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Mint" title="New Orleans Mint">
        New Orleans Mint
       </a>
       , a former branch of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Mint" title="United States Mint">
        United States Mint
       </a>
       which now operates as a museum, and
       <a href="/wiki/The_Historic_New_Orleans_Collection" title="The Historic New Orleans Collection">
        The Historic New Orleans Collection
       </a>
       , a museum and research center housing art and artifacts relating to the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_Orleans" title="History of New Orleans">
        history
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_South" title="Gulf South">
        Gulf South
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Close to the Quarter is the
       <a href="/wiki/Trem%C3%A9" title="Tremé">
        Tremé
       </a>
       community, which contains the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Jazz_National_Historical_Park" title="New Orleans Jazz National Historical Park">
        New Orleans Jazz National Historical Park
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_African_American_Museum" title="New Orleans African American Museum">
        New Orleans African American Museum
       </a>
       — a site which is listed on the
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_African_American_Heritage_Trail" title="Louisiana African American Heritage Trail">
        Louisiana African American Heritage Trail
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Natchez_(boat)" title="Natchez (boat)">
         Natchez
        </a>
       </i>
       is an authentic
       <a href="/wiki/Steamboat" title="Steamboat">
        steamboat
       </a>
       with a
       <a href="/wiki/Calliope_(music)" title="Calliope (music)">
        calliope
       </a>
       that cruises the length of the city twice daily. Unlike most other places in the United States, New Orleans has become widely known for its
       <a href="/wiki/Elegant_decay" title="Elegant decay">
        elegant decay
       </a>
       . The city's historic cemeteries and their distinct above-ground
       <a href="/wiki/Tomb" title="Tomb">
        tombs
       </a>
       are attractions in themselves, the oldest and most famous of which,
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Louis_Cemetery" title="Saint Louis Cemetery">
        Saint Louis Cemetery
       </a>
       , greatly resembles
       <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A8re_Lachaise_Cemetery" title="Père Lachaise Cemetery">
        Père Lachaise Cemetery
       </a>
       in Paris.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NOMAReopeningDayDelgadoFascade.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/NOMAReopeningDayDelgadoFascade.jpg/235px-NOMAReopeningDayDelgadoFascade.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/NOMAReopeningDayDelgadoFascade.jpg/353px-NOMAReopeningDayDelgadoFascade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/NOMAReopeningDayDelgadoFascade.jpg/470px-NOMAReopeningDayDelgadoFascade.jpg 2x" width="235"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NOMAReopeningDayDelgadoFascade.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Museum_of_Art" title="New Orleans Museum of Art">
          New Orleans Museum of Art
         </a>
         (NOMA) located in
         <a href="/wiki/City_Park,_New_Orleans" title="City Park, New Orleans">
          City Park
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/The_National_WWII_Museum" title="The National WWII Museum">
        The National WWII Museum
       </a>
       offers a multi-building odyssey through the history of the Pacific and European theaters. Nearby,
       <a href="/wiki/Confederate_Memorial_Hall" title="Confederate Memorial Hall">
        Confederate Memorial Hall
       </a>
       , the oldest continually-operating museum in Louisiana (although under renovation since Katrina), contains the second-largest collection of
       <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">
        Confederate
       </a>
       memorabilia. Art museums include the
       <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_Arts_Center_(New_Orleans)" title="Contemporary Arts Center (New Orleans)">
        Contemporary Arts Center
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Museum_of_Art" title="New Orleans Museum of Art">
        New Orleans Museum of Art
       </a>
       (NOMA) in
       <a href="/wiki/City_Park_(New_Orleans)" title="City Park (New Orleans)">
        City Park
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Ogden_Museum_of_Southern_Art" title="Ogden Museum of Southern Art">
        Ogden Museum of Southern Art
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans is home to the
       <a href="/wiki/Audubon_Nature_Institute" title="Audubon Nature Institute">
        Audubon Nature Institute
       </a>
       (which consists of
       <a href="/wiki/Audubon_Park,_New_Orleans" title="Audubon Park, New Orleans">
        Audubon Park
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Audubon_Zoo" title="Audubon Zoo">
        Audubon Zoo
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Aquarium_of_the_Americas" title="Aquarium of the Americas">
        Aquarium of the Americas
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audubon_Insectarium" title="Audubon Insectarium">
        Audubon Insectarium
       </a>
       ), and home to gardens which include
       <a href="/wiki/Longue_Vue_House_and_Gardens" title="Longue Vue House and Gardens">
        Longue Vue House and Gardens
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Botanical_Garden" title="New Orleans Botanical Garden">
        New Orleans Botanical Garden
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/City_Park_(New_Orleans)" title="City Park (New Orleans)">
        City Park
       </a>
       , one of the country's most expansive and visited
       <a href="/wiki/Urban_park" title="Urban park">
        urban parks
       </a>
       , has one of the largest stands of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_live_oak" title="Southern live oak">
        oak trees
       </a>
       in the world.
      </p>
      <p>
       Other points of interest can be found in the surrounding areas. Many wetlands are found nearby, including
       <a href="/wiki/Honey_Island_Swamp" title="Honey Island Swamp">
        Honey Island Swamp
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lafitte_National_Historical_Park_and_Preserve#Barataria_Preserve" title="Jean Lafitte National Historical Park and Preserve">
        Barataria Preserve
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lafitte_National_Historical_Park_and_Preserve#Chalmette_unit" title="Jean Lafitte National Historical Park and Preserve">
        Chalmette Battlefield and National Cemetery
       </a>
       , located just south of the city, is the site of the 1815
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_New_Orleans" title="Battle of New Orleans">
        Battle of New Orleans
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2009, New Orleans ranked No. 7 on
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Newsmax" title="Newsmax">
         Newsmax
        </a>
       </i>
       magazine's list of the "Top 25 Most Uniquely American Cities and Towns". The piece cited the city's post-Katrina rebuilding effort as well as its efforts to become eco-friendly.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
        <a href="#cite_note-138">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment_and_performing_arts">
        Entertainment and performing arts
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_New_Orleans" title="Music of New Orleans">
        Music of New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MardiGrasCanalStreet1890sChartresGazebo.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="488" data-file-width="640" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/MardiGrasCanalStreet1890sChartresGazebo.jpg/235px-MardiGrasCanalStreet1890sChartresGazebo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/MardiGrasCanalStreet1890sChartresGazebo.jpg/353px-MardiGrasCanalStreet1890sChartresGazebo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/MardiGrasCanalStreet1890sChartresGazebo.jpg/470px-MardiGrasCanalStreet1890sChartresGazebo.jpg 2x" width="235"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MardiGrasCanalStreet1890sChartresGazebo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Mardi_Gras" title="New Orleans Mardi Gras">
          New Orleans Mardi Gras
         </a>
         in the early 1890s.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ToHorses.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="276" data-file-width="466" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/ToHorses.jpg/235px-ToHorses.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/ToHorses.jpg/353px-ToHorses.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5d/ToHorses.jpg 2x" width="235"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ToHorses.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Mounted
         <a href="/wiki/Krewe" title="Krewe">
          krewe
         </a>
         officers in the Thoth Parade during
         <a href="/wiki/Mardi_Gras" title="Mardi Gras">
          Mardi Gras
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The New Orleans area is home to numerous annual celebrations. The most well-known is
       <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">
        Carnival
       </a>
       , or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Mardi_Gras" title="New Orleans Mardi Gras">
        Mardi Gras
       </a>
       . Carnival officially begins on the
       <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">
        Feast of the Epiphany
       </a>
       , also known as the "
       <a href="/wiki/Twelfth_Night_(holiday)" title="Twelfth Night (holiday)">
        Twelfth Night
       </a>
       ". Mardi Gras (French for "Fat Tuesday"), the final and grandest day of festivities, is the last Tuesday before the
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
        Catholic
       </a>
       liturgical season of
       <a href="/wiki/Lent" title="Lent">
        Lent
       </a>
       , which commences on
       <a href="/wiki/Ash_Wednesday" title="Ash Wednesday">
        Ash Wednesday
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The largest of the city's many music festivals is the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Jazz_%26_Heritage_Festival" title="New Orleans Jazz &amp; Heritage Festival">
        New Orleans Jazz &amp; Heritage Festival
       </a>
       . Commonly referred to simply as "Jazz Fest", it is one of the nation's largest music festivals. The festival features a variety of music, including both native Louisiana and international artists. Along with Jazz Fest, New Orleans'
       <a href="/wiki/Voodoo_Experience" title="Voodoo Experience">
        Voodoo Experience
       </a>
       ("Voodoo Fest") and the
       <a href="/wiki/Essence_Music_Festival" title="Essence Music Festival">
        Essence Music Festival
       </a>
       are other festivals featuring local and international artists.
      </p>
      <p>
       Other major festivals include
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Decadence" title="Southern Decadence">
        Southern Decadence
       </a>
       , the French Quarter Festival and the
       <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Williams/New_Orleans_Literary_Festival" title="Tennessee Williams/New Orleans Literary Festival">
        Tennessee Williams/New Orleans Literary Festival
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2002, Louisiana began offering tax incentives for film and television production. This led to a substantial increase in activity and brought the nickname "Hollywood South." Films produced in and around New Orleans include
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ray_(film)" title="Ray (film)">
         Ray
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Runaway_Jury" title="Runaway Jury">
         Runaway Jury
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Pelican_Brief_(film)" title="The Pelican Brief (film)">
         The Pelican Brief
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Glory_Road_(film)" title="Glory Road (film)">
         Glory Road
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/All_the_King%27s_Men_(2006_film)" title="All the King's Men (2006 film)">
         All the King's Men
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deja_Vu_(2006_film)" title="Deja Vu (2006 film)">
         Déjà Vu
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Last_Holiday_(2006_film)" title="Last Holiday (2006 film)">
         Last Holiday
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Curious_Case_of_Benjamin_Button_(film)" title="The Curious Case of Benjamin Button (film)">
         The Curious Case of Benjamin Button
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/12_Years_a_Slave_(film)" title="12 Years a Slave (film)">
         12 Years a Slave
        </a>
       </i>
       . In 2006, work began on the Louisiana Film &amp; Television studio complex, based in
       <a href="/wiki/Trem%C3%A9" title="Tremé">
        Tremé
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
        <a href="#cite_note-139">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Louisiana began to offer similar tax incentives for music and theater productions in 2007, leading many to begin referring to New Orleans as "Broadway South."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
        <a href="#cite_note-140">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The first theatre in New Orleans was the French-language
       <a href="/wiki/Theatre_de_la_Rue_Saint_Pierre" title="Theatre de la Rue Saint Pierre">
        Theatre de la Rue Saint Pierre
       </a>
       , which opened in 1792. The first opera in New Orleans was performed there in 1796. In the nineteenth century the city was the home of two of America's most important venues for
       <a href="/wiki/French_opera" title="French opera">
        French opera
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_d%27Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Théâtre d'Orléans">
        Théâtre d'Orléans
       </a>
       and later the
       <a href="/wiki/French_Opera_House" title="French Opera House">
        French Opera House
       </a>
       . Today, opera is performed by the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Opera" title="New Orleans Opera">
        New Orleans Opera
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louis_Armstrong_restored.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2912" data-file-width="3738" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Louis_Armstrong_restored.jpg/200px-Louis_Armstrong_restored.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Louis_Armstrong_restored.jpg/300px-Louis_Armstrong_restored.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Louis_Armstrong_restored.jpg/400px-Louis_Armstrong_restored.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louis_Armstrong_restored.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armstrong" title="Louis Armstrong">
          Louis Armstrong
         </a>
         , famous New Orleans
         <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">
          jazz
         </a>
         musician
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frank_Ocean.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1326" data-file-width="1895" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Frank_Ocean.jpg/200px-Frank_Ocean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Frank_Ocean.jpg/300px-Frank_Ocean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Frank_Ocean.jpg/400px-Frank_Ocean.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Frank_Ocean.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Frank_Ocean" title="Frank Ocean">
          Frank Ocean
         </a>
         is a musician from New Orleans.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans has long been a significant center for music, showcasing its intertwined European, Latin American and African cultures. The city's unique musical heritage was born in its colonial and early American days from a unique blending of European musical instruments with African rhythms. As the only North American city to have allowed
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">
        slaves
       </a>
       to gather in public and play their native music (largely in
       <a href="/wiki/Congo_Square" title="Congo Square">
        Congo Square
       </a>
       , now located within
       <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armstrong_Park_(New_Orleans)" title="Louis Armstrong Park (New Orleans)">
        Louis Armstrong Park
       </a>
       ), New Orleans gave birth to an epochal indigenous music:
       <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">
        jazz
       </a>
       . Soon,
       <a href="/wiki/Brass_band" title="Brass band">
        brass bands
       </a>
       formed, beginning a century-long tradition. The Louis Armstrong Park area, near the French Quarter in
       <a href="/wiki/Trem%C3%A9" title="Tremé">
        Tremé
       </a>
       , contains the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Jazz_National_Historical_Park" title="New Orleans Jazz National Historical Park">
        New Orleans Jazz National Historical Park
       </a>
       . The city's music was later significantly influenced by
       <a href="/wiki/Acadiana" title="Acadiana">
        Acadiana
       </a>
       , home of
       <a href="/wiki/Cajun_music" title="Cajun music">
        Cajun
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Zydeco" title="Zydeco">
        Zydeco
       </a>
       music, and by
       <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">
        Delta blues
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans' unique musical culture is on display in its traditional funerals. A spin on military funerals, New Orleans' traditional funerals feature sad music (mostly
       <a href="/wiki/Dirge" title="Dirge">
        dirges
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hymn" title="Hymn">
        hymns
       </a>
       ) on the way to the cemetery and happier music (hot jazz) on the way back. Until the 1990s, most locals preferred to call these "funerals with music", but visitors to the city have long dubbed them "
       <a href="/wiki/Jazz_funeral" title="Jazz funeral">
        jazz funerals
       </a>
       ."
      </p>
      <p>
       Much later in its musical development, New Orleans was home to a distinctive brand of
       <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">
        rhythm and blues
       </a>
       that contributed greatly to the growth of
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">
        rock and roll
       </a>
       . An example of the New Orleans' sound in the 1960s is the #1 US hit "
       <a href="/wiki/Chapel_of_Love" title="Chapel of Love">
        Chapel of Love
       </a>
       " by
       <a href="/wiki/The_Dixie_Cups" title="The Dixie Cups">
        the Dixie Cups
       </a>
       , a song which knocked
       <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">
        the Beatles
       </a>
       out of the top spot on the
       <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">
        Billboard Hot 100
       </a>
       . New Orleans became a hotbed for
       <a href="/wiki/Funk" title="Funk">
        funk
       </a>
       music in the 1960s and 1970s, and by the late 1980s, it had developed its own localized variant of
       <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">
        hip hop
       </a>
       , called
       <a href="/wiki/Bounce_music" title="Bounce music">
        bounce music
       </a>
       . While not commercially successful outside of the
       <a href="/wiki/Deep_South" title="Deep South">
        Deep South
       </a>
       , it remained immensely popular in poorer neighborhoods throughout the 1990s.
      </p>
      <p>
       A cousin of bounce,
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_hip_hop" title="Southern hip hop">
        New Orleans hip hop
       </a>
       achieved commercial success locally and internationally, producing
       <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">
        Lil Wayne
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Master_P" title="Master P">
        Master P
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Birdman_(rapper)" title="Birdman (rapper)">
        Birdman
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_(rapper)" title="Juvenile (rapper)">
        Juvenile
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cash_Money_Records" title="Cash Money Records">
        Cash Money Records
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/No_Limit_Records" title="No Limit Records">
        No Limit Records
       </a>
       . Additionally, the popularity of
       <a href="/wiki/Cowpunk" title="Cowpunk">
        cowpunk
       </a>
       , a fast form of
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_rock" title="Southern rock">
        southern rock
       </a>
       , originated with the help of several local bands, such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Radiators_(US)" title="The Radiators (US)">
        The Radiators
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Better_Than_Ezra" title="Better Than Ezra">
        Better Than Ezra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cowboy_Mouth" title="Cowboy Mouth">
        Cowboy Mouth
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Dash_Rip_Rock" title="Dash Rip Rock">
        Dash Rip Rock
       </a>
       . Throughout the 1990s, many
       <a href="/wiki/Sludge_metal" title="Sludge metal">
        sludge metal
       </a>
       bands started. New Orleans'
       <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">
        heavy metal
       </a>
       bands like
       <a href="/wiki/Eyehategod" title="Eyehategod">
        Eyehategod
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMG-Eyehategod_141-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AMG-Eyehategod-141">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Soilent_Green" title="Soilent Green">
        Soilent Green
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMG-SoilentGreen_142-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AMG-SoilentGreen-142">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crowbar_(US_band)" title="Crowbar (US band)">
        Crowbar
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMG-Crowbar_143-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AMG-Crowbar-143">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Down_(band)" title="Down (band)">
        Down
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMG-Down_144-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AMG-Down-144">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
       incorporated styles such as
       <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_punk" title="Hardcore punk">
        hardcore punk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Doom_metal" title="Doom metal">
        doom metal
       </a>
       and southern rock to create an original and heady brew of swampy and aggravated metal that has largely avoided standardization.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMG-Eyehategod_141-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-AMG-Eyehategod-141">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMG-SoilentGreen_142-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-AMG-SoilentGreen-142">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMG-Crowbar_143-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-AMG-Crowbar-143">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMG-Down_144-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-AMG-Down-144">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans is the southern terminus of the famed
       <a href="/wiki/Highway_61_Revisited#Highway_61" title="Highway 61 Revisited">
        Highway 61
       </a>
       made musically famous by
       <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">
        Bob Dylan
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Food">
        Food
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steamship_Bienville_on-board_restaurant_menu_(April_7,_1861).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="599" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Steamship_Bienville_on-board_restaurant_menu_%28April_7%2C_1861%29.jpg/200px-Steamship_Bienville_on-board_restaurant_menu_%28April_7%2C_1861%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Steamship_Bienville_on-board_restaurant_menu_%28April_7%2C_1861%29.jpg/300px-Steamship_Bienville_on-board_restaurant_menu_%28April_7%2C_1861%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Steamship_Bienville_on-board_restaurant_menu_%28April_7%2C_1861%29.jpg/400px-Steamship_Bienville_on-board_restaurant_menu_%28April_7%2C_1861%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steamship_Bienville_on-board_restaurant_menu_(April_7,_1861).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Steamship Bienville on-board restaurant menu (April 7, 1861)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cafe_du_Monde_New_Orleans.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1168" data-file-width="1760" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Cafe_du_Monde_New_Orleans.jpg/200px-Cafe_du_Monde_New_Orleans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Cafe_du_Monde_New_Orleans.jpg/300px-Cafe_du_Monde_New_Orleans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Cafe_du_Monde_New_Orleans.jpg/400px-Cafe_du_Monde_New_Orleans.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cafe_du_Monde_New_Orleans.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_du_Monde" title="Café du Monde">
          Café du Monde
         </a>
         , a landmark New Orleans beignet cafe established in 1862.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_New_Orleans" title="Cuisine of New Orleans">
        Cuisine of New Orleans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Creole_cuisine" title="Louisiana Creole cuisine">
        Louisiana Creole cuisine
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cajun_cuisine" title="Cajun cuisine">
        Cajun cuisine
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans is world-famous for its food. The indigenous cuisine is distinctive and influential. New Orleans food combined local Creole, haute Creole and New Orleans French cuisines. Local ingredients, French, Spanish, Italian, African, Native American, Cajun, Chinese, and a hint of Cuban traditions combine to produce a truly unique and easily recognizable New Orleans flavor.
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans is known for specialties including
       <a href="/wiki/Beignet" title="Beignet">
        beignets
       </a>
       (locally pronounced like "ben-yays"), square-shaped fried dough that could be called "French doughnuts" (served with
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_au_lait" title="Café au lait">
         café au lait
        </a>
       </i>
       made with a blend of coffee and chicory rather than only coffee); and
       <a href="/wiki/Po%27_boy" title="Po' boy">
        po' boy
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
        <a href="#cite_note-145">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and Italian
       <a href="/wiki/Muffuletta" title="Muffuletta">
        muffuletta
       </a>
       sandwiches; Gulf oysters on the half-shell, fried oysters, boiled
       <a href="/wiki/Crayfish" title="Crayfish">
        crawfish
       </a>
       and other
       <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">
        seafood
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%89touff%C3%A9e" title="Étouffée">
        étouffée
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jambalaya" title="Jambalaya">
        jambalaya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gumbo" title="Gumbo">
        gumbo
       </a>
       and other Creole dishes; and the Monday favorite of
       <a href="/wiki/Red_beans_and_rice" title="Red beans and rice">
        red beans and rice
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armstrong" title="Louis Armstrong">
        Louis Armstrong
       </a>
       often signed his letters, "Red beans and ricely yours"). Another New Orleans specialty is the
       <a href="/wiki/Praline" title="Praline">
        praline
       </a>
       <span class="nowrap">
        <small>
         locally
        </small>
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'p' in 'pie'">
            p
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">
            ɑː
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">
            iː
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       , a candy made with brown sugar, granulated sugar, cream, butter, and pecans. The city offers notable street food
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
        <a href="#cite_note-146">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
       including the Asian inspired beef
       <a href="/wiki/Yaka_mein" title="Yaka mein">
        Yaka mein
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dialect">
        Dialect
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_English" title="New Orleans English">
        New Orleans English
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_New_Orleans#Language" title="Culture of New Orleans">
        Culture of New Orleans § Language
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans ceveloped a distinctive local dialect that is neither
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cajun" title="Cajun">
        Cajun
       </a>
       nor the stereotypical
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_American_English" title="Southern American English">
        Southern
       </a>
       accent that is often misportrayed by film and television actors. Like earlier Southern Englishes, feature frequent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhotic_and_non-rhotic_accents" title="Rhotic and non-rhotic accents">
        deletion of the pre-consonantal "r"
       </a>
       . This dialect is quite similar to New York City area accents such as "
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_English" title="New York City English">
        Brooklynese
       </a>
       ", to people unfamiliar with either.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
        <a href="#cite_note-147">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
       No consensus describes how it came to be, but it likely resulted from New Orleans' geographic isolation by water and the fact that the city was a major immigration port throughout the 19th century. As a result, many of the ethnic groups who reside in Brooklyn also reside in New Orleans, such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">
        Irish
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">
        Italians
       </a>
       (especially
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sicilian_American" title="Sicilian American">
        Sicilians
       </a>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">
        Germans
       </a>
       and a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_American" title="Jewish American">
        Jewish
       </a>
       community.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
        <a href="#cite_note-148">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       One of the strongest varieties of the New Orleans accent is sometimes identified as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yat_dialect" title="Yat dialect">
        Yat dialect
       </a>
       , from the greeting "Where y'at?" This distinctive accent is dying out in the city, but remains strong in the surrounding parishes.
      </p>
      <p>
       Less visibly, various ethnic groups throughout the area have retained distinct language traditions. Although rare, languages still spoken include
       <a href="/wiki/Cajun_French" title="Cajun French">
        Cajun
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louisiana_Creole_French" title="Louisiana Creole French">
        Kreyol Lwiziyen
       </a>
       spoken by the
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Creole_people" title="Louisiana Creole people">
        Creoles
       </a>
       and an archaic Louisiana-Canarian Spanish dialect spoken by the
       <a href="/wiki/Isle%C3%B1o" title="Isleño">
        Isleño
       </a>
       people and older members of the population.
      </p>
