        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Shrine_on_Airline" title="Shrine on Airline">
          Shrine on Airline
         </a>
         (10,000)
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         1993
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         14
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         11,012
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       New Orleans' professional sports teams include the 2009
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLIV" title="Super Bowl XLIV">
        Super Bowl XLIV
       </a>
       champion
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Saints" title="New Orleans Saints">
        New Orleans Saints
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">
        NFL
       </a>
       ), the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Pelicans" title="New Orleans Pelicans">
        New Orleans Pelicans
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">
        NBA
       </a>
       ), and the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Baby_Cakes" title="New Orleans Baby Cakes">
        New Orleans Baby Cakes
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_League" title="Pacific Coast League">
        PCL
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
        <a href="#cite_note-149">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is also home to the
       <a href="/wiki/Big_Easy_Rollergirls" title="Big Easy Rollergirls">
        Big Easy Rollergirls
       </a>
       , an all-female
       <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Flat_Track_Derby_Association" title="Women's Flat Track Derby Association">
        flat track roller derby
       </a>
       team, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Blaze" title="New Orleans Blaze">
        New Orleans Blaze
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/National_Women%27s_Football_Association" title="National Women's Football Association">
        women's football
       </a>
       team.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BlazeFootball_150-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BlazeFootball-150">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BERG_151-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BERG-151">
         [148]
        </a>
       </sup>
       New Orleans is also home to two
       <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">
        NCAA Division I
       </a>
       athletic programs, the
       <a href="/wiki/Tulane_Green_Wave" title="Tulane Green Wave">
        Tulane Green Wave
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Athletic_Conference" title="American Athletic Conference">
        American Athletic Conference
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNO_Privateers" title="UNO Privateers">
        UNO Privateers
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Southland_Conference" title="Southland Conference">
        Southland Conference
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fleur_de_lys_(or).svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="214" data-file-width="150" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Fleur_de_lys_%28or%29.svg/100px-Fleur_de_lys_%28or%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Fleur_de_lys_%28or%29.svg/150px-Fleur_de_lys_%28or%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Fleur_de_lys_%28or%29.svg/200px-Fleur_de_lys_%28or%29.svg.png 2x" width="100"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fleur_de_lys_(or).svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Fleur-de-lis" title="Fleur-de-lis">
          fleur-de-lis
         </a>
         is often a symbol of New Orleans and its sports teams.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Superdome" title="Mercedes-Benz Superdome">
        Mercedes-Benz Superdome
       </a>
       is the home of the Saints, the Sugar Bowl, and other prominent events. It has hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">
        Super Bowl
       </a>
       a record seven times (
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XII" title="Super Bowl XII">
        1978
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XV" title="Super Bowl XV">
        1981
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XX" title="Super Bowl XX">
        1986
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXIV" title="Super Bowl XXIV">
        1990
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXI" title="Super Bowl XXXI">
        1997
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXVI" title="Super Bowl XXXVI">
        2002
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVII" title="Super Bowl XLVII">
        2013
       </a>
       ). The
       <a href="/wiki/Smoothie_King_Center" title="Smoothie King Center">
        Smoothie King Center
       </a>
       is the home of the Pelicans, VooDoo, and many events that are not large enough to need the Superdome. New Orleans is also home to the
       <a href="/wiki/Fair_Grounds_Race_Course" title="Fair Grounds Race Course">
        Fair Grounds Race Course
       </a>
       , the nation's third-oldest thoroughbred track. The city's
       <a href="/wiki/Lakefront_Arena" title="Lakefront Arena">
        Lakefront Arena
       </a>
       has also been home to sporting events.
      </p>
      <p>
       Each year New Orleans plays host to the
       <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Bowl" title="Sugar Bowl">
        Sugar Bowl
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Bowl" title="New Orleans Bowl">
        New Orleans Bowl
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Classic_of_New_Orleans" title="Zurich Classic of New Orleans">
        Zurich Classic
       </a>
       , a golf tournament on the
       <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour" title="PGA Tour">
        PGA Tour
       </a>
       . In addition, it has often hosted major sporting events that have no permanent home, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">
        Super Bowl
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/ArenaBowl" title="ArenaBowl">
        ArenaBowl
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/NBA_All-Star_Game" title="NBA All-Star Game">
        NBA All-Star Game
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/BCS_National_Championship_Game" title="BCS National Championship Game">
        BCS National Championship Game
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">
        NCAA Final Four
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_%E2%80%98n%E2%80%99_Roll_Mardi_Gras_Marathon" title="Rock ‘n’ Roll Mardi Gras Marathon">
        Rock ‘n’ Roll Mardi Gras Marathon
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Crescent_City_Classic" title="Crescent City Classic">
        Crescent City Classic
       </a>
       are two annual
       <a href="/wiki/Road_running" title="Road running">
        road running
       </a>
       events.
      </p>

      <div style="clear:left;">
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">
        Government
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_New_Orleans" title="List of mayors of New Orleans">
        List of mayors of New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            verification
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_Orleans&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (May 2009)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The City is a political subdivision of the state of Louisiana. It has a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayor-council_government" title="Mayor-council government">
        mayor-council government
       </a>
       , following a
       <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">
        Home Rule
       </a>
       Charter adopted in 1954, as later amended. The
       <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">
        city council
       </a>
       consists of seven members, who are elected by district and two at-large councilmembers. The mayor as of 2017 was
       <a href="/wiki/Mitch_Landrieu" title="Mitch Landrieu">
        Mitch Landrieu
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
        <a href="#cite_note-152">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
        <a href="#cite_note-153">
         [150]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Orleans_Parish_Sheriff%27s_Office_(Louisiana)" title="Orleans Parish Sheriff's Office (Louisiana)">
        Orleans Parish Civil Sheriff's Office
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Service_of_process" title="Service of process">
        serves
       </a>
       papers involving lawsuits and provides security for the Civil District Court and Juvenile Courts. The
       <a href="/wiki/Orleans_Parish_Sheriff%27s_Office_(Louisiana)#The_Sheriff" title="Orleans Parish Sheriff's Office (Louisiana)">
        Criminal Sheriff, Marlin Gusman
       </a>
       , maintains the parish prison system, provides security for the Criminal District Court, and provides backup for the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Police_Department" title="New Orleans Police Department">
        New Orleans Police Department
       </a>
       on an as-needed basis. An ordinance in 2006 established an
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Office_of_Inspector_General" title="New Orleans Office of Inspector General">
        Office of Inspector General
       </a>
       to review city government activities.
      </p>
      <p>
       The city and the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_parishes_in_Louisiana" title="List of parishes in Louisiana">
        parish
       </a>
       of Orleans operate as a merged
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consolidated_city%E2%80%93county" title="Consolidated city–county">
        city-parish government
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR6_154-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-GR6-154">
         [151]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The original city was composed of what are now the 1st through 9th wards. The city of Lafayette (including the Garden District) was added in 1852 as the 10th and 11th wards. In 1870, Jefferson City, including Faubourg Bouligny and much of the Audubon and University areas, was annexed as the 12th, 13th, and 14th wards.
       <a href="/wiki/Algiers,_New_Orleans" title="Algiers, New Orleans">
        Algiers
       </a>
       , on the west bank of the Mississippi, was also annexed in 1870, becoming the 15th ward.
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans' government is largely centralized in the city council and mayor's office, but it maintains earlier systems from when various sections of the city managed their affairs separately. For example, New Orleans had seven elected tax assessors, each with their own staff, representing various districts of the city, rather than one centralized office. A constitutional amendment passed on November 7, 2006 consolidated the seven assessors into one in 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
        <a href="#cite_note-155">
         [152]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The New Orleans government operates both a
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Fire_Department" title="New Orleans Fire Department">
        fire department
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Emergency_Medical_Services" title="New Orleans Emergency Medical Services">
        New Orleans Emergency Medical Services
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">
        Crime
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Murder_Capitol">
        Murder Capitol
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Police_Department" title="New Orleans Police Department">
        New Orleans Police Department
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_New_Orleans#Crime" title="Culture of New Orleans">
        Culture of New Orleans § Crime
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Crime is an ongoing problem. As in comparable U.S. cities, the incidence of homicide and other violent crimes is highly concentrated in certain impoverished neighborhoods.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ritea_156-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ritea-156">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The murder rate for the city has been historically high and consistently among the highest rates nationwide.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
        <a href="#cite_note-157">
         [154]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1994 New Orleans was named "Murder Capitol of America" as the city hit a historic peak of 424 killings. The murder count surpassed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_D.C." title="Washington D.C.">
        Washington D.C.
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
        Chicago
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">
        Baltimore
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">
        Miami
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
        <a href="#cite_note-158">
         [155]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2003 New Orleans's murder rate was nearly eight times the national average—and since then, murder has increased. In 2002 and 2003, New Orleans once again had the highest per capita city homicide rate in the United States with 274 homicides up from the previous year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
        <a href="#cite_note-159">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
        <a href="#cite_note-160">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the FBI New Orleans was officially ranked the "America's Murder Capitol" for the second time since 1994.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
        <a href="#cite_note-161">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Homicides peaked in the early to mid 1990's at 86 murders per 100,000 residents.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
        <a href="#cite_note-162">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 2009, despite a 17% decrease in violent crime, the homicide rate remained among the highest
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
        <a href="#cite_note-163">
         [160]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in the United States, at between 55 and 64 per 100,000 residents.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
        <a href="#cite_note-164">
         [161]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2010, New Orleans was 49.1 per 100,000, and in 2012, that number climbed to 53.2.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-city-data.com_165-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-city-data.com-165">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
        <a href="#cite_note-166">
         [163]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was the highest rate among cities of 250,000 population or larger.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
        <a href="#cite_note-167">
         [164]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Offenders in New Orleans are almost exclusively black males: 97% were black and 95% were male.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
        <a href="#cite_note-168">
         [165]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The violent crime rate was a key issue in the 2010 mayoral race. In January 2007, several thousand New Orleans residents marched to City Hall for a rally demanding police and city leaders tackle the crime problem. Then-Mayor
       <a href="/wiki/Ray_Nagin" title="Ray Nagin">
        Ray Nagin
       </a>
       said he was "totally and solely focused" on addressing the problem. Later, the city implemented checkpoints during late night hours in problem areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
        <a href="#cite_note-169">
         [166]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The murder rate climbed 14% in 2011 to 57.88 per 100,000
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
        <a href="#cite_note-170">
         [167]
        </a>
       </sup>
       rising to #21 in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
        <a href="#cite_note-171">
         [168]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2016, according to annual crime statistics released by the New Orleans Police Department, 176 were murdered.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
        <a href="#cite_note-172">
         [169]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
        <a href="#cite_note-173">
         [170]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-city-data.com_165-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-city-data.com-165">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2017 New Orleans had the highest rate and of gun violence surpassing the large populated
       <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
        Chicago
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
        <a href="#cite_note-174">
         [171]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
        <a href="#cite_note-175">
         [172]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">
        Colleges and universities
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibson_Hall.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Gibson_Hall.jpg/250px-Gibson_Hall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Gibson_Hall.jpg/375px-Gibson_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Gibson_Hall.jpg/500px-Gibson_Hall.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibson_Hall.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A view of Gibson Hall at
         <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">
          Tulane University
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Several higher education institutions operate there:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">
         Tulane University
        </a>
        , a major
        <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">
         research university
        </a>
        founded in 1834.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Loyola_University_New_Orleans" title="Loyola University New Orleans">
         Loyola University New Orleans
        </a>
        , a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">
         Jesuit
        </a>
        university founded in 1912.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_Orleans" title="University of New Orleans">
         University of New Orleans
        </a>
        , a large public research university.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Xavier_University_of_Louisiana" title="Xavier University of Louisiana">
         Xavier University of Louisiana
        </a>
        , the only historically black Catholic university in the United States.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Southern_University_at_New_Orleans" title="Southern University at New Orleans">
         Southern University at New Orleans
        </a>
        , an historically black university in the
        <a href="/wiki/Southern_University_System" title="Southern University System">
         Southern University System
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Dillard_University" title="Dillard University">
         Dillard University
        </a>
        , a private, historically black liberal arts college founded in 1869.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/LSU_Health_Sciences_Center_New_Orleans" title="LSU Health Sciences Center New Orleans">
         Louisiana State University Health Sciences Center
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Holy_Cross_College" title="Our Lady of Holy Cross College">
         Our Lady of Holy Cross College
        </a>
        , a Catholic liberal arts college founded in 1916.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Seminary" title="Notre Dame Seminary">
         Notre Dame Seminary
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Baptist_Theological_Seminary" title="New Orleans Baptist Theological Seminary">
         New Orleans Baptist Theological Seminary
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Delgado_Community_College" title="Delgado Community College">
         Delgado Community College
        </a>
        , founded in 1921.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_Carey_College#School_of_Nursing" title="William Carey College">
         William Carey College School of Nursing
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herzing_College" title="Herzing College">
         Herzing College
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        New Orleans Culinary Institute
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_schools">
        Primary and secondary schools
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Public_Schools" title="New Orleans Public Schools">
        New Orleans Public Schools
       </a>
       (NOPS) is the city's public school system. Katrina was a watershed moment for the school system. Pre-Katrina, NOPS was one of the area's largest systems (along with the
       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Parish_Public_Schools" title="Jefferson Parish Public Schools">
        Jefferson Parish public school system
       </a>
       ). It was also the lowest-performing school district in Louisiana. According to researchers
       <a href="/wiki/Carl_L._Bankston" title="Carl L. Bankston">
        Carl L. Bankston
       </a>
       and Stephen J. Caldas, only 12 of the 103 public schools within the city limits showed reasonably good performance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
        <a href="#cite_note-176">
         [173]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Following Hurricane Katrina, the state of Louisiana took over most of the schools within the system (all schools that matched a nominal "worst-performing" metric). Many of these schools (and others) were subsequently granted operating charters giving them administrative independence from the Orleans Parish School Board, the
       <a href="/wiki/Recovery_School_District" title="Recovery School District">
        Recovery School District
       </a>
       and/or the
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Board_of_Elementary_and_Secondary_Education" title="Louisiana Board of Elementary and Secondary Education">
        Louisiana Board of Elementary and Secondary Education
       </a>
       (BESE). At the start of the 2014 school year, all public school students in the NOPS system attended these independent
       <a href="/wiki/Charter_school" title="Charter school">
        public charter schools
       </a>
       , the nation's first to do so.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
        <a href="#cite_note-177">
         [174]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The charter schools made significant and sustained gains in student achievement, led by outside operators such as
       <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_Is_Power_Program" title="Knowledge Is Power Program">
        KIPP
       </a>
       , the Algiers Charter School Network, and the Capital One – University of New Orleans Charter School Network. An October 2009 assessment demonstrated continued growth in the academic performance of public schools. Considering the scores of all public schools in New Orleans gives an overall school district performance score of 70.6. This score represents a 24% improvement over an equivalent pre-Katrina (2004) metric, when a district score of 56.9 was posted.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
        <a href="#cite_note-178">
         [175]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Notably, this score of 70.6 approaches the score (78.4) posted in 2009 by the adjacent, suburban
       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Parish_Public_Schools" title="Jefferson Parish Public Schools">
        Jefferson Parish public school system
       </a>
       , though that system's performance score is itself below the state average of 91.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
        <a href="#cite_note-179">
         [176]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       One particular change was that parents could
       <a href="/wiki/School_choice#United_States" title="School choice">
        choose which school to enroll their children in
       </a>
       , rather than attending the school nearest them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Times-Picayune_2009_180-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-The_Times-Picayune_2009-180">
         [177]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">
        Libraries
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Academic and
       <a href="/wiki/Public_library" title="Public library">
        public libraries
       </a>
       as well as archives in New Orleans include
       <a href="/wiki/Loyola_University_New_Orleans#Monroe_Library" title="Loyola University New Orleans">
        Monroe Library
       </a>
       at Loyola University, Howard-Tilton Memorial Library at
       <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">
        Tulane University
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
        <a href="#cite_note-181">
         [178]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the Law Library of Louisiana,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
        <a href="#cite_note-182">
         [179]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Earl_Long" title="Earl Long">
        Earl K. Long
       </a>
       Library at the University of New Orleans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
        <a href="#cite_note-183">
         [180]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Public_Library" title="New Orleans Public Library">
        New Orleans Public Library
       </a>
       operates in 13 locations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">
        <a href="#cite_note-184">
         [181]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The main library includes a Louisiana Division that houses city archives and special collections.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">
        <a href="#cite_note-185">
         [182]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Other research archives are located at
       <a href="/wiki/The_Historic_New_Orleans_Collection" title="The Historic New Orleans Collection">
        the Historic New Orleans Collection
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">
        <a href="#cite_note-186">
         [183]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Mint" title="New Orleans Mint">
        Old U.S. Mint
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187">
        <a href="#cite_note-187">
         [184]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       An independently operated lending library called
       <a href="/wiki/Iron_Rail_Book_Collective" title="Iron Rail Book Collective">
        Iron Rail Book Collective
       </a>
       specializes in radical and hard-to-find books. The library contains over 8,000 titles and is open to the public.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Historical_Association" title="Louisiana Historical Association">
        Louisiana Historical Association
       </a>
       was founded in New Orleans in 1889. It operated first at Howard Memorial Library. A separate Memorial Hall for it was later added to Howard Library, designed by New Orleans architect
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Sully_(architect)" title="Thomas Sully (architect)">
        Thomas Sully
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
        <a href="#cite_note-188">
         [185]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Media_of_New_Orleans" title="Media of New Orleans">
        Media of New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_New_Orleans#News_&amp;_entertainment_media" title="Culture of New Orleans">
        Culture of New Orleans § News &amp; entertainment media
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Historically, the major newspaper in the area was
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Times-Picayune" title="The Times-Picayune">
         The Times-Picayune
        </a>
       </i>
       . The paper made headlines of its own in 2012 when owner
       <a href="/wiki/Advance_Publications" title="Advance Publications">
        Advance Publications
       </a>
       cut its print schedule to three days each week, instead focusing its efforts on its website, NOLA.com. That action briefly made New Orleans the largest city in the country without a daily newspaper, until the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge" title="Baton Rouge">
        Baton Rouge
       </a>
       newspaper
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Advocate_(Louisiana)" title="The Advocate (Louisiana)">
         The Advocate
        </a>
       </i>
       began a New Orleans edition in September 2012. In June 2013, the
       <i>
        Times-Picayune
       </i>
       resumed daily printing with a condensed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newsstand" title="Newsstand">
        newsstand
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_(newspaper_format)" title="Tabloid (newspaper format)">
        tabloid
       </a>
       edition, nicknamed
       <i>
        TP Street
       </i>
       , which is published on the three days each week that its namesake
       <a href="/wiki/Broadsheet" title="Broadsheet">
        broadsheet
       </a>
       edition is not printed (the Picayune has not returned to daily delivery). With the resumption of daily print editions from the
       <i>
        Times-Picayune
       </i>
       and the launch of the New Orleans edition of
       <i>
        The Advocate
       </i>
       , now
       <i>
        The New Orleans Advocate
       </i>
       , the city had two daily newspapers for the first time since the afternoon States-Item ceased publication on May 31, 1980.
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to the daily newspapers, weekly publications include
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Louisiana_Weekly" title="The Louisiana Weekly">
         The Louisiana Weekly
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gambit_Weekly" title="Gambit Weekly">
         Gambit Weekly
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189">
        <a href="#cite_note-189">
         [186]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also, in wide circulation is the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Clarion_Herald" title="Clarion Herald">
         Clarion Herald
        </a>
       </i>
       , the newspaper of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_New_Orleans" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of New Orleans">
        Roman Catholic Archdiocese of New Orleans
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Greater New Orleans is the 54th largest
       <a href="/wiki/Media_market" title="Media market">
        Designated Market Area
       </a>
       (DMA) in the U.S., serving 566,960 homes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
        <a href="#cite_note-190">
         [187]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Major television network affiliates serving the area include:
      </p>
      <div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-3" style="-moz-column-count: 3; -webkit-column-count: 3; column-count: 3;">
       <ul>
        <li>
         4
         <a href="/wiki/WWL-TV" title="WWL-TV">
          WWL
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">
          CBS
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         6
         <a href="/wiki/WDSU" title="WDSU">
          WDSU
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">
          NBC
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         8
         <a href="/wiki/WVUE-DT" title="WVUE-DT">
          WVUE
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">
          Fox
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         12
         <a href="/wiki/WYES-TV" title="WYES-TV">
          WYES
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">
          PBS
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         20
         <a href="/wiki/WHNO" title="WHNO">
          WHNO
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Lester_Sumrall" title="Lester Sumrall">
          LeSEA
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         26
         <a href="/wiki/WGNO" title="WGNO">
          WGNO
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">
          ABC
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         32
         <a href="/wiki/WLAE-TV" title="WLAE-TV">
          WLAE
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">
          PBS
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         38
         <a href="/wiki/WNOL-TV" title="WNOL-TV">
          WNOL
         </a>
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_CW_Television_Network" title="The CW Television Network">
          The CW
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         42
         <a href="/wiki/KGLA-DT" title="KGLA-DT">
          KGLA
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Telemundo" title="Telemundo">
          Telemundo
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         49
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WPXL" title="WPXL">
          WPXL
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Ion_Television" title="Ion Television">
          Ion
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         54
         <a href="/wiki/WUPL" title="WUPL">
          WUPL
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/MyNetworkTV" title="MyNetworkTV">
          MyNetworkTV
         </a>
         )
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <p>
       WWOZ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
        <a href="#cite_note-191">
         [188]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the New Orleans Jazz and Heritage Station, broadcasts,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">
        <a href="#cite_note-192">
         [189]
        </a>
       </sup>
       modern and traditional jazz, blues, rhythm and blues, brass band,
       <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">
        gospel
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cajun_music" title="Cajun music">
        cajun
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Zydeco" title="Zydeco">
        zydeco
       </a>
       , Caribbean, Latin, Brazilian, African and bluegrass 24 hours per day.
      </p>
      <p>
       WTUL,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
        <a href="#cite_note-193">
         [190]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is the Tulane University radio station. Its programming includes 20th century classical, reggae, jazz, showtunes, indie rock, electronic music, soul/funk, goth, punk, hip hop, New Orleans music, opera, folk, hardcore,
       <a href="/wiki/Americana_(music)" title="Americana (music)">
        Americana
       </a>
       , country, blues, Latin, cheese, techno, local, world, ska, swing and big band, kids shows, and news programming. WTUL is listener supported and non-commercial. The disc jockeys are volunteers, many of them college students.
      </p>
      <p>
       Louisiana's film and television tax credits spurred growth in the television industry, although to a lesser degree than in the film industry. Many films and advertisements were set there, along with television programs such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Real_World:_New_Orleans" title="The Real World: New Orleans">
         The Real World: New Orleans
        </a>
       </i>
       in 2000,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nola.com_194-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nola.com-194">
         [191]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Real_World:_Back_to_New_Orleans" title="The Real World: Back to New Orleans">
         The Real World: Back to New Orleans
        </a>
       </i>
       in 2009 and 2010
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195">
        <a href="#cite_note-195">
         [192]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196">
        <a href="#cite_note-196">
         [193]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Bad_Girls_Club_(season_7)" title="Bad Girls Club (season 7)">
         Bad Girls Club: New Orleans
        </a>
       </i>
       in 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197">
        <a href="#cite_note-197">
         [194]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Two
       <a href="/wiki/Radio_broadcasting" title="Radio broadcasting">
        radio stations
       </a>
       that were influential in promoting New Orleans-based bands and singers were 50,000-watt WNOE-AM (1060) and 10,000-watt
       <a href="/wiki/WQNO" title="WQNO">
        WTIX
       </a>
       (690 AM). These two stations competed head-to-head from the late 1950s to the late 1970s.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Streetcars">
        Streetcars
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CanalSt3Oct07PT922MB.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/CanalSt3Oct07PT922MB.jpg/225px-CanalSt3Oct07PT922MB.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/CanalSt3Oct07PT922MB.jpg/338px-CanalSt3Oct07PT922MB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/CanalSt3Oct07PT922MB.jpg/450px-CanalSt3Oct07PT922MB.jpg 2x" width="225"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CanalSt3Oct07PT922MB.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A New Orleans
         <a href="/wiki/Streetcars_in_New_Orleans" title="Streetcars in New Orleans">
          streetcar
         </a>
         traveling down Canal Street
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Orlean_Streetcars.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/New_Orlean_Streetcars.svg/225px-New_Orlean_Streetcars.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/New_Orlean_Streetcars.svg/338px-New_Orlean_Streetcars.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/New_Orlean_Streetcars.svg/450px-New_Orlean_Streetcars.svg.png 2x" width="225"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Orlean_Streetcars.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Streetcar network
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Streetcars_in_New_Orleans" title="Streetcars in New Orleans">
        Streetcars in New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans has four active
       <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">
        streetcar lines
       </a>
       :
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/St._Charles_Streetcar_Line" title="St. Charles Streetcar Line">
          St. Charles Streetcar Line
         </a>
        </b>
        is the oldest continuously operating streetcar line in America. Each car is a historic landmark. It runs from Canal Street to the other end of St. Charles Avenue, then turns right into South Carrolton Avenue to its terminal at Carrolton and Claiborne.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Riverfront_Streetcar_Line" title="Riverfront Streetcar Line">
          Riverfront Streetcar Line
         </a>
        </b>
        runs parallel to the river from Esplanade Street through the French Quarter to Canal Street to the Convention Center above Julia Street in the Arts District.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Canal_Streetcar_Line" title="Canal Streetcar Line">
          Canal Streetcar Line
         </a>
        </b>
        uses the Riverfront line tracks from the intersection of Canal Street and Poydras Street, down Canal Street, then branches off and ends at the cemeteries at City Park Avenue, with a spur running from the intersection of Canal and Carrollton Avenue to the entrance of City Park at Esplanade, near the entrance to the New Orleans Museum of Art.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Rampart%E2%80%93St._Claude_Streetcar_Line" title="Rampart–St. Claude Streetcar Line">
          Rampart–St. Claude Streetcar Line
         </a>
        </b>
        opened on January 28, 2013 as the
        <i>
         Loyola-UPT Line
        </i>
        running along Loyola Avenue from
        <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Union_Passenger_Terminal" title="New Orleans Union Passenger Terminal">
         New Orleans Union Passenger Terminal
        </a>
        to Canal Street, then continuing along Canal Street to the river, and on weekends on the Riverfront line tracks to French Market. The French Quarter Rail Expansion extended the line from the Loyola Avenue/Canal Street intersection along Rampart Street and St. Claude Avenue to Elysian Fields Avenue. It no longer runs along Canal Street to the river, or on weekends on the Riverfront line tracks to French Market.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The city's streetcars were featured in the
       <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Williams" title="Tennessee Williams">
        Tennessee Williams
       </a>
       play,
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Streetcar_Named_Desire_(play)" title="A Streetcar Named Desire (play)">
         A Streetcar Named Desire
        </a>
       </i>
       . The streetcar line to Desire Street became a bus line in 1948.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycling">
        Bicycling
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The city's flat landscape, simple street grid, and mild winters, facilitate
       <a href="/wiki/Bicycle" title="Bicycle">
        bicycle
       </a>
       ridership, helping to make New Orleans eighth among U.S. cities in its rate of bicycle and
       <a href="/wiki/Pedestrian" title="Pedestrian">
        pedestrian
       </a>
       transportation as of 2010,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_198-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-198">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and sixth in terms of the percentage of bicycling commuters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_199-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-199">
         [196]
        </a>
       </sup>
       New Orelans is located at the start of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River_Trail" title="Mississippi River Trail">
        Mississippi River Trail
       </a>
       , a 3,000-mile (4,800 km) bicycle path that stretches from the city's
       <a href="/wiki/Audubon_Park,_New_Orleans" title="Audubon Park, New Orleans">
        Audubon Park
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">
        Minnesota
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200">
        <a href="#cite_note-200">
         [197]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since Katrina the city has actively sought to promote bicycling by constructing a $1.5 million bike trail from
       <a href="/wiki/Mid-City_New_Orleans" title="Mid-City New Orleans">
        Mid-City
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pontchartrain" title="Lake Pontchartrain">
        Lake Pontchartrain
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201">
        <a href="#cite_note-201">
         [198]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and by adding over 37 miles (60 km) of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicycle_lane" title="Bicycle lane">
        bicycle lanes
       </a>
       to various streets, including
       <a href="/wiki/St._Charles_Avenue" title="St. Charles Avenue">
        St. Charles Avenue
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_198-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-198">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2009,
       <a href="/wiki/Tulane_University" title="Tulane University">
        Tulane University
       </a>
       contributed to these efforts by converting the main street through its
       <a href="/wiki/Uptown_New_Orleans" title="Uptown New Orleans">
        Uptown
       </a>
       campus,
       <a href="/wiki/McAlister_Place,_New_Orleans" title="McAlister Place, New Orleans">
        McAlister Place
       </a>
       , into a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedestrian_mall" title="Pedestrian mall">
        pedestrian mall
       </a>
       opened to bicycle traffic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
        <a href="#cite_note-202">
         [199]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A 3.1-mile (5.0 km) bicycle corridor stretches from the French Quarter to Lakeview, and 14 miles (23 km) of additional bike lanes on existing streets.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_199-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-199">
         [196]
        </a>
       </sup>
       New Orleans has been recognized for its abundance of uniquely decorated and uniquely designed bicycles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
        <a href="#cite_note-203">
         [200]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">
        Buses
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">
        Public transportation
       </a>
       is operated by the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Regional_Transit_Authority" title="New Orleans Regional Transit Authority">
        New Orleans Regional Transit Authority
       </a>
       ("RTA"). Many
       <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">
        bus
       </a>
       routes connect the city and suburban areas. The RTA lost 200+ buses in the flood. Some of the replacement buses operate on
       <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">
        biodiesel
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Jefferson Parish, Louisiana">
        Jefferson Parish
       </a>
       Department of Transit Administration
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
        <a href="#cite_note-204">
         [201]
        </a>
       </sup>
       operates Jefferson Transit, which provides service between the city and its suburbs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205">
        <a href="#cite_note-205">
         [202]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">
        Roads
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_streets_of_New_Orleans" title="List of streets of New Orleans">
        List of streets of New Orleans
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans is served by
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_10" title="Interstate 10">
        Interstate 10
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_610_(Louisiana)" title="Interstate 610 (Louisiana)">
        Interstate 610
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_510" title="Interstate 510">
        Interstate 510
       </a>
       . I-10 travels east–west through the city as the
       <a href="/wiki/Pontchartrain_Expressway" title="Pontchartrain Expressway">
        Pontchartrain Expressway
       </a>
       . In
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_New_Orleans" title="Eastern New Orleans">
        New Orleans East
       </a>
       it is known as the Eastern Expressway. I-610 provides a direct shortcut for traffic passing through New Orleans via I-10, allowing that traffic to bypass I-10's southward curve.
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to the interstates,
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_90" title="U.S. Route 90">
        U.S. 90
       </a>
       travels through the city, while
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_61" title="U.S. Route 61">
        U.S. 61
       </a>
       terminates downtown. In addition,
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_11" title="U.S. Route 11">
        U.S. 11
       </a>
       terminates in the eastern portion of the city.
      </p>
      <p>
       New Orleans is home to many bridges, most notably
       <a href="/wiki/Crescent_City_Connection" title="Crescent City Connection">
        Crescent City Connection
       </a>
       is perhaps the most notable. It serves as New Orleans' major bridge across the Mississippi, providing a connection between the city's downtown on the eastbank and its westbank suburbs. Other Mississippi crossings are the
       <a href="/wiki/Huey_P._Long_Bridge_(Jefferson_Parish)" title="Huey P. Long Bridge (Jefferson Parish)">
        Huey P. Long Bridge
       </a>
       , carrying U.S. 90 and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luling_Bridge" title="Luling Bridge">
        Hale Boggs Memorial Bridge
       </a>
       , carrying
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_310" title="Interstate 310">
        Interstate 310
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/I-10_Twin_Span_Bridge" title="I-10 Twin Span Bridge">
        Twin Span Bridge
       </a>
       , a five-mile (8 km)
       <a href="/wiki/Causeway" title="Causeway">
        causeway
       </a>
       in eastern New Orleans, carries I-10 across Lake Pontchartrain. Also in eastern New Orleans,
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_510" title="Interstate 510">
        Interstate 510
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Highway_47" title="Louisiana Highway 47">
        LA 47
       </a>
       travels across the
       <a href="/wiki/Intracoastal_Waterway" title="Intracoastal Waterway">
        Intracoastal Waterway
       </a>
       /
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mississippi_River-Gulf_Outlet_Canal" title="Mississippi River-Gulf Outlet Canal">
        Mississippi River-Gulf Outlet Canal
       </a>
       via the
       <a href="/wiki/Green_Bridge_(New_Orleans)" title="Green Bridge (New Orleans)">
        Paris Road Bridge
       </a>
       , connecting
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_New_Orleans" title="Eastern New Orleans">
        New Orleans East
       </a>
       and suburban
       <a href="/wiki/Chalmette,_Louisiana" title="Chalmette, Louisiana">
        Chalmette
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The tolled
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pontchartrain_Causeway" title="Lake Pontchartrain Causeway">
        Lake Pontchartrain Causeway
       </a>
       , consisting of two parallel bridges are, at 24 miles (39 km) long, the longest bridges in the world. Built in the 1950s (southbound span) and 1960s (northbound span), the bridges connect New Orleans with its suburbs on the north shore of Lake Pontchartrain via
       <a href="/wiki/Metairie,_Louisiana" title="Metairie, Louisiana">
        Metairie
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">
        Airports
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The metropolitan area is served by the
       <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armstrong_New_Orleans_International_Airport" title="Louis Armstrong New Orleans International Airport">
        Louis Armstrong New Orleans International Airport
       </a>
       , located in the suburb of
       <a href="/wiki/Kenner,_Louisiana" title="Kenner, Louisiana">
        Kenner
       </a>
       . Regional airports include the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Lakefront_Airport" title="New Orleans Lakefront Airport">
        Lakefront Airport
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Joint_Reserve_Base_New_Orleans" title="Naval Air Station Joint Reserve Base New Orleans">
        Naval Air Station Joint Reserve Base New Orleans
       </a>
       (Callender Field) in the suburb of Belle Chasse and
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Seaplane_Airport" title="Southern Seaplane Airport">
        Southern Seaplane Airport
       </a>
       , also located in Belle Chasse. Southern Seaplane has a 3,200-foot (980 m) runway for wheeled planes and a 5,000-foot (1,500 m) water runway for seaplanes. New Orleans International suffered some damage from Katrina, but as of April 2007, it was the busiest airport in Louisiana and the sixth busiest in the Southeast. As of 2017, the airport handled more than 11 million passengers, serving more than 57 destinations. The airport's international service includes nonstop flights to the United Kingdom, Germany, Canada, Mexico, Honduras, Bahamas and Dominican Republic.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">
        Rail
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The city is served by
       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
        Amtrak
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Union_Passenger_Terminal" title="New Orleans Union Passenger Terminal">
        New Orleans Union Passenger Terminal
       </a>
       is the central rail depot and is served by the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crescent_(Amtrak)" title="Crescent (Amtrak)">
         Crescent
        </a>
       </i>
       , operating between New Orleans and New York City; the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/City_of_New_Orleans_(train)" title="City of New Orleans (train)">
         City of New Orleans
        </a>
       </i>
       , operating between New Orleans and Chicago and the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Limited" title="Sunset Limited">
         Sunset Limited
        </a>
       </i>
       , operating through New Orleans between
       <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">
        Orlando
       </a>
       and Los Angeles. Beginning in late August 2005, the Sunset Limited no longer served its official route. Since late October 2005 served only New Orleans-to-Los Angeles. The obstacles to restoration of the full route have been more managerial and political than physical.
      </p>
      <p>
       With the strategic benefits of both the port and its double-track Mississippi River crossings, the city attracted six of the seven
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_I_railroad" title="Class I railroad">
        Class I railroads
       </a>
       in North America:
       <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">
        Union Pacific Railroad
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/BNSF_Railway" title="BNSF Railway">
        BNSF Railway
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern_Railway" title="Norfolk Southern Railway">
        Norfolk Southern Railway
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Southern_Railway" title="Kansas City Southern Railway">
        Kansas City Southern Railway
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">
        CSX Transportation
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_National_Railway" title="Canadian National Railway">
        Canadian National Railway
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Public_Belt_Railroad" title="New Orleans Public Belt Railroad">
        New Orleans Public Belt Railroad
       </a>
       provides interchange services between the railroads.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ferries">
        Ferries
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AlgiersFerry_TJefferson_arriving3_bright.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/AlgiersFerry_TJefferson_arriving3_bright.jpg/250px-AlgiersFerry_TJefferson_arriving3_bright.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/AlgiersFerry_TJefferson_arriving3_bright.jpg/375px-AlgiersFerry_TJefferson_arriving3_bright.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/AlgiersFerry_TJefferson_arriving3_bright.jpg/500px-AlgiersFerry_TJefferson_arriving3_bright.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AlgiersFerry_TJefferson_arriving3_bright.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Ferries connecting New Orleans with
         <a href="/wiki/Algiers,_New_Orleans" title="Algiers, New Orleans">
          Algiers
         </a>
         (left) and Gretna (right)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Orleans has had continuous ferry service since 1827, operating three routes as of 2017. The
       <a href="/wiki/Canal_Street_Ferry" title="Canal Street Ferry">
        Canal Street Ferry
       </a>
       (or Algiers Ferry) connects downtown New Orleans at the foot of
       <a href="/wiki/Canal_Street,_New_Orleans" title="Canal Street, New Orleans">
        Canal Street
       </a>
       with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark_District" title="National Historic Landmark District">
        National Historic Landmark District
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Algiers_Point" title="Algiers Point">
        Algiers Point
       </a>
       across the Mississippi ("West Bank" in local parlance). It services passenger vehicles, bicycles and pedestrians. This same terminal also serves the Canal Street/Gretna Ferry, connecting
       <a href="/wiki/Gretna,_Louisiana" title="Gretna, Louisiana">
        Gretna, Louisiana
       </a>
       for pedestrians and bicyclists only. A third auto/bicycle/pedestrian connects
       <a href="/wiki/Chalmette,_Louisiana" title="Chalmette, Louisiana">
        Chalmette, Louisiana
       </a>
       and Lower Algiers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-friendsoftheferry.org_206-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-friendsoftheferry.org-206">
         [203]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">

       </a>
      </div>

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Twinnings_and_Partnerships">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">
        See also
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
       <ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
        Notes
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references">
         <li id="cite_note-73">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-73">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Mean monthly maxima and minima (i.e. the expected highest and lowest temperature readings at any point during the year or given month) calculated based on data at said location from 1981 to 2010.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-75">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-75">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Official records for New Orleans have been kept at MSY since 1 May 1946.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
            <a href="#cite_note-74">
             [73]
            </a>
           </sup>
           Additional records from Audubon Park dating back to 1893 have also been included.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-76">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-76">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Sunshine normals are based on only 20 to 22 years of data
          </span>
         </li>
        </ol>

        <li id="cite_note-mostunique-14">

          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-mostunique_14-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          The term "most unique" is grammatically incorrect, as the word "unique" is a
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/superlative" title="wikt:superlative">
           superlative
          </a>
          . See for example:
          <br/>
          <i>
           Merriam-Webster Dictionary of American Usage
          </i>
          , Springfield, Massachusetts: Merriam-Webster, Inc., 1994.
          <br/>
          Fowler, Henry,
          <i>
           A Dictionary of Modern English Usage
          </i>
          , Oxford: Oxford University Press, USA, 2003.
          <br/>
          Nicholson, Margaret,
          <i>
           A Dictionary of American English Usage
          </i>
          , New York: Oxford University Press, 1957.
         </span>

          <cite class="citation web">

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Batumi+City+Hall&amp;rft.atitle=Batumi+%E2%80%93+Twin+Towns+%26+Sister+Cities&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.batumi.ge%2Fen%2F%3Fpage%3Dshow%26sec%3D5&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANew+Orleans">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
       </ol>
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">
        Further reading
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <cite class="citation book" id="CITEREFGitlin2009">
         Gitlin, Jay (1 December 2009).
         <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=x4P2TI_mfsQC&amp;pg=PA159" rel="nofollow">
          <i>
           The Bourgeois Frontier: French Towns, French Traders, and American Expansion
          </i>
         </a>
         . Yale University Press. p. 159.
         <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
          ISBN
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-300-15576-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-300-15576-1">
          978-0-300-15576-1
         </a>
         .
        </cite>
        <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Bourgeois+Frontier%3A+French+Towns%2C+French+Traders%2C+and+American+Expansion&amp;rft.pages=159&amp;rft.pub=Yale+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2009-12-01&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-300-15576-1&amp;rft.aulast=Gitlin&amp;rft.aufirst=Jay&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dx4P2TI_mfsQC%26pg%3DPA159&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANew+Orleans">
         <span style="display:none;">
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Thomas J. Adams and Steve Striffler (eds.),
        <i>
         Working in the Big Easy: The History and Politics of Labor in New Orleans.
        </i>
        Lafayette, Louisiana: University of Louisiana at Lafayette Press, 2014.
       </li>
       <li>
        Nathalie Dessens,
        <i>
         Creole City: A Chronicle of Early American New Orleans.
        </i>
        Gainesville, Florida: University Press of Florida, 2015.
       </li>
       <li>
        Rien Fertel,
        <i>
         Imagining the Creole City: The Rise of Literary Culture in Nineteenth-Century New Orleans.
        </i>
        Baton Rouge, Louisiana: Louisiana State University Press, 2014.
       </li>
       <li>
        Scott P. Marler,
        <i>
         The Merchants' Capital: New Orleans and the Political Economy of the Nineteenth-Century South.
        </i>
        New York: Cambridge University Press, 2013.
       </li>
       <li>
        Lawrence N. Powell,
        <i>
         The Accidental City: Improvising New Orleans.
        </i>
        Cambridge, Massachusetts: Harvard University Press, 2012.
       </li>
       <li>
        LaKisha Michelle Simmons,
        <i>
         Crescent City Girls: The Lives of Young Black Women in Segregated New Orleans.
        </i>
        Chapel Hill, NC: University of North Carolina Press, 2015.
       </li>
       <li>
        Rebecca Solnit and Rebecca Snedeker,
        <i>
         Unfathomable City: A New Orleans Atlas.
        </i>
        Berkeley, California: University of California Press, 2013.
       </li>
      </ul>
